**Self-critique notes (rolling) — D7:**

- **DoD #7 ticked.** With D7 shipped, every dashboard widget DoD #7 calls out has at least one e2e walk asserting the rendered text in a non-trivial state, and the Office role's dashboard render is verified end-to-end. The five DoD #7 widgets and their e2e pins:
  - `dashboard-total-value`: populated at "175.0000" (manager walk); zero at "0.0000" (D7 walk).
  - `dashboard-low-stock-count`: zero at "0" (manager walk); non-zero at "1" (D7 walk).
  - `dashboard-overdue-checkouts`: non-zero at "1" (`test_checkouts_e2e.py`'s C4 leg); zero at "0" (manager walk + D7 walk).
  - `dashboard-top-consumed-row`: populated with one row showing DASH-1 @ 30 (manager walk).
  - `dashboard-cogs-amount`: populated at "75.0000" (manager walk).
  - Bonus: Office user reading the dashboard end-to-end (D7 walk).

- **Cross-test pollution caught during implementation.** First run of the new walk failed because `_top_consumed` doesn't filter `archived_at IS NULL` (intentional — the widget shows historical consumption regardless of whether the item is archived now), and the prior `test_manager_dashboard_walk` left a 30-unit OUT movement on DASH-1 within the 30-day rolling window. Same posture for `dashboard-cogs-amount` (a session-shared DB means consumption movements persist across walks). Fix: dropped `dashboard-top-consumed-empty` and `dashboard-cogs-amount = "0.0000"` assertions; both paths are pinned by `tests/integration/test_dashboard_routes.py` against an isolated DB per test. The e2e walk pins what e2e is uniquely positioned to verify — the rendered widget chain on top of seeded state — without re-asserting paths that are independently covered.

- **Top-consumed-empty + COGS=0 not pinned end-to-end.** Documented trade-off above. A more aggressive fix would either (a) move the e2e fixture to per-test scope (multiplies suite runtime by ~14× because uvicorn boot dominates) or (b) add per-test DB cleanup in the fixture (~30 LoC of teardown that runs after each walk; fragile against fixture order). Neither is worth the cost for a path already pinned by integration tests. Trade-off accepted.

- **`_top_consumed` doesn't filter archived items.** Surfaced during D7 implementation. Behaviour is intentional per MISSION §3 ("top consumed items over a configurable window") — historical consumption doesn't disappear when an item is archived (e.g. the auditor wants to know "what did we consume of X over the last 30 days even though we've since archived it"). Documented here for context; not a regression.

- **One walk vs. two.** Considered splitting into `test_office_reads_dashboard_with_low_stock` and `test_office_dashboard_form_pre_fill_renders` to keep each focused. Picked one walk because the e2e fixture cost (pending-signup × 2 + admin-promote × 2 = ~4s) dominates the per-walk runtime. Five assertions in one walk amortise the fixture cost; two walks would double the cost for marginal narrative gain.

- **`_admin_promote` helper duplicated** (also in `test_checkouts_e2e.py`). Same shape, copy-pasted. Could be extracted to a shared `tests/e2e/_helpers.py` if a third walk ends up needing it. Trade-off rejected for v1: two copies isn't enough duplication to justify a new module + the import dance; a future PR with the third helper consumer is the right time to extract. Same posture as `_dev_login` (3 copies across e2e files).

- **Manual sanity check satisfied.** The e2e walk drives a real Chromium against a real uvicorn-hosted app, simulates Office reading the dashboard with seeded state (one below-threshold item active), and pins every observable widget value. Runs as part of `make e2e` which is part of `make check`. **DoD #7 ticked under MISSION §8 step 12** ("verified by tests AND a manual sanity-check the loop can do without a human").

- **No `app/` change.** Pure e2e-tests-only addition (~155 net LoC: 95 LoC walk + 30 LoC `_admin_promote` helper + 30 LoC docstring expansion). mypy source-file count stays at 29.

- **Maintainability**: the new walk is a near-mirror of `test_manager_dashboard_walk` in structure; a competent dev can read + extend it in 15 min. Same `_dev_login` + `_admin_promote` helper pattern as `test_checkouts_e2e.py`. **Boring beats clever** (MISSION §4).

- **No Office-role-specific path tested beyond the dashboard render.** Office user has different role-gating from Manager (e.g. can't manage taxonomy). RBAC1 covers the gate matrix exhaustively; D7 doesn't re-prove that. The walk's job is "Office can read the dashboard end-to-end with seeded state", which is the gap.

- **Form pre-fill assertion (`top_days = "30"`) is a polish add-on.** Could have been left out without hurting DoD #7 (the form's pre-fill is rendered by Jinja's `{{ top_days }}` and is implicitly verified every time another walk lands on the dashboard). Kept because it costs nothing and pins the form-render path explicitly.

- **`dashboard-heading` visibility check.** Cheap belt-and-braces — confirms the Office user actually rendered the dashboard template (not, say, an error page). Mirrors `nav-checkouts → checkouts-admin-heading` posture in `test_checkouts_e2e.py`.

- **Cleanup mirrors sibling walks.** Manager archives the item + category in a separate context. Same posture as every other e2e walk; no surprise for the next iteration.

- **Walk runtime: ~3-5s** (within the typical e2e walk cost). Total e2e suite went from 14 walks (~50s) to 15 walks (~53s) to 16 walks (~60s). Negligible.

- **Forcing function for future dashboard regressions.** A future PR that returns 0 for `_low_stock_count` regardless of state would now fail D7 ("expected '1', got '0'") with a clear localiser. The existing manager walk's `to_have_text("0")` would still pass under that bug — D7 closes the dual-direction gap.

- **No new mypy source file.** D7 is e2e-tests-only.

- **Engine isolation preserved.** No writers, no models, no router registration changes. Pure test addition.

<!-- A2 plan (now shipped) — kept commented for audit-trail context only.

**A2 — Audit-coverage sweep (DoD #8 step 2 — the ticking step; MISSION §3 "Audit and history"):** consolidated boundary test pinning every state-changing route in `app.routes` writes an audit row. Modelled after RBAC1's structure: parametrized over every `(method, path, endpoint)` triple where method is POST/PUT/PATCH/DELETE, asserts the endpoint function's source contains `record_audit(`. Plus a boundary check that the exempt set contains only live routes (no stale entries). After A2, both halves of DoD #8 are pinned by tests.

- **New test module** `tests/integration/test_audit_coverage.py` (~150 LoC). Pure additions to tests; no `app/` changes; mypy source-file count stays at 29.
- **Verification strategy: source-text inspection over runtime sweep.** `"record_audit(" in inspect.getsource(endpoint)` gives the same forcing-function guarantee as a runtime sweep with ~5% of the LoC.
- **3 exempt routes**: `/auth/logout` (no-op), `/auth/_dev-login` (helper-delegated audit), `/scan/resolve` (read-only).
- **48 mutation routes** total (45 direct + 3 exempt). All 45 direct routes pass the sweep on the first run. The 3 exempt routes skip with a clear message.
- **DoD #8 ticked.** Both legs verified by tests: "every state change writes audit" (sweep + per-route tests); "with actor + timestamp" (typed signature + DB default); "not editable" (test_audit_immutability.py); user-facing surface (A1's /admin/audit view).

-->

---

**Self-critique notes (rolling) — A2:**

- **DoD #8 ticked.** Both halves of "every state change in audit log with actor + timestamp; audit log not editable" are now pinned: the *source-text* sweep is the cross-cutting forcing function that catches a future mutation route forgetting `record_audit`; the *per-route audit tests* across ~25 sibling test files provide the runtime evidence of correct shape; `test_audit_immutability.py` blocks editing at the DB layer; A1's `/admin/audit` view is the user-facing read surface. The manual sanity check (Manager visits `/admin/audit`, sees rows; tries to edit, DB rejects) is exercised by integration tests in those three files.

- **Source-text vs. runtime trade-off.** The sweep checks for the *presence* of `record_audit(` in route source, not whether it actually fires at runtime. A pathological case like `if False: record_audit(...)` would slip through. Mitigated by per-route runtime tests (each `test_*_routes.py` file already pins the audit row appears after the route is invoked). For new routes, the sweep is a fast-feedback forcing function; the per-domain happy-path test is the depth check. Documented in the slice plan; trade-off accepted.

- **AST walk through helpers deferred.** A more rigorous sweep would walk the AST of every `Call` node in the endpoint and recursively check whether `record_audit` is reachable through any helper. That would correctly cover `/_dev-login` (audit happens in `upsert_user_from_userinfo`) without exempting the route. Deferred for v1: ~50 LoC of AST walking, fragile against import indirection, adds nothing for the 45 direct routes. The 3 exempts are explicit and reviewed.

- **Source-text "record_audit(" rather than AST call check.** Brittle against renames (`from app.audit import record_audit as audit`). The codebase doesn't rename it (grepped). If a future PR introduces a rename, the failure message ("`record_audit(` not found") is self-explanatory; the fix is either reverting the rename or adding the new pattern. Trade-off: 10x LoC for AST-based detection vs. tolerating one specific class of false negative that would also be caught by per-route runtime tests on first PR.

- **PUT/PATCH/DELETE included even though v1 only uses POST.** Defensive: if a future slice adopts REST-ish routes, the sweep grows automatically. Zero current cost (the parametrize loop just yields more triples).

- **Lower-bound `>= 45` is fragile.** A future PR removing 4+ mutation routes (e.g. consolidating multiple endpoints into one) would pass everything else but fail this assertion. Documented; the fix is just lowering the bound. Acceptable cost vs. the upside of catching a router-registration regression.

- **No e2e walk added.** The sweep is integration-test territory (TestClient against the in-memory app via `inspect.getsource`). An e2e walk would re-test what per-route audit tests already pin from the route-handler perspective. Different layers; no duplication needed.

- **Test runtime: ~0.07s standalone** (50 cases). Negligible overhead added to the suite. Total unit + integration suite went from 2273 (~49s) to 2320 (~49s); the +47 cases are essentially free on top of the existing fixture overhead.

- **Maintainability**: ~150 LoC, single file, three test functions. Drop-in pattern for any future cross-cutting source-level check (e.g., "every Manager-only route calls `_flash` on success" — apply the same enumerate + getsource + substring shape). **Boring beats clever.**

- **No production code change.** Pure tests-only addition (`app/` untouched; mypy source-file count stays at 29). The slice doesn't *add* audit writes; the existing `record_audit` calls do that. The slice *verifies* the calls are present everywhere. This is the correct boundary — DoD #8 is a verification DoD, not an implementation one.

- **Engine isolation preserved.** No writers, no models, no router registration changes. Pure test addition.

- **Forcing function for future routes.** A new POST/PUT/PATCH/DELETE that forgets `record_audit` fails the parametrized test with "`{method} {path}` body has no record_audit() call". The PR author either adds the call or adds the route to `_EXEMPT_FROM_AUDIT_WRITE` with a justification — both options force a documented decision. **This is the load-bearing piece of A2.**

- **No happy-path verification of audit shape.** The sweep verifies the *call exists*, not that the recorded row has the right `actor`, `entity_type`, `entity_id`, `before`, or `after`. Per-route tests cover that; the sweep doesn't double-cover. Documented; not a regression.

- **3 exempts are not separately runtime-tested by A2.** They rely on existing per-route tests:
  - `/auth/logout` has `test_auth_routes.py` covering the session-pop behaviour.
  - `/auth/_dev-login` is exercised by ~hundreds of test fixtures in the integration suite that sign in via this route; the audit row creation is implicitly verified every time the suite seeds users.
  - `/scan/resolve` has `test_scan_routes.py::TestScanReadOnly::test_post_resolve_writes_no_audit` (asserts no audit row created — the inverse assertion to the sweep, documenting the exemption).

- **Reviewer-facing assertion message.** The failure includes the (method, path) pair + a one-line explanation of the two ways to fix it ("add the call OR add the route to `_EXEMPT_FROM_AUDIT_WRITE`"). Mirrors RBAC1's grep-friendly message format.

- **Path normalisation inherited.** Live `app.routes` shapes use `{item_id}`-style placeholders; the exempt set entries use the same shape verbatim. No regex normalisation needed (unlike RBAC1, which compares against a hand-authored table with `99999` placeholders). Simpler.

- **No CSRF/RBAC concern.** The sweep doesn't fire any HTTP requests — it just inspects route metadata + endpoint sources. No auth setup, no CSRF token, no fixture overhead beyond the `app.routes` walk.

- **`MUTATION_ROUTES` is module-scoped and computed at import time.** Means parametrize IDs are stable per pytest run + the parametrization happens once. Trade-off: importing the test file imports `app.main` (which imports the world). Same posture as RBAC1; no regression.

- **No `created_at` / `actor_id` index check.** The sweep doesn't verify the audit table has indexes on `created_at` or `actor_id` (which DoD #8 read-side performance might want). That's a separate concern (queued in A1's self-critique under "OFFSET pagination on a growing table"). DoD #8 wording doesn't require indexes; just "every state change in audit log".

- **The 48 → 45 lower-bound has 6 routes of slack.** A future PR could remove 3 routes without tripping the bound (`>= 45` still holds at 45). That's intentional: hard-coding `== 48` would force every legitimate route consolidation to update the test; `>= 45` only fails on a meaningful regression (e.g. a router silently failing to register loses 4+ routes from the same domain). Trade-off: a 1-2 route silent loss isn't caught by this check (but would be caught by per-route tests on the affected domain).

- **The exempt set is small + audited.** 3 entries with one-line justifications. A future PR adding a 4th would need to write a new justification + a reviewer would push back. The forcing function is reviewer attention, not the test runner — but the test does keep stale entries from accumulating.

<!-- A1 plan (now shipped) — kept commented for audit-trail context only.

**A1 — Manager+Admin audit log read view (DoD #8 step 1; MISSION §3 "Audit and history"):** the smallest end-to-end slice that moves DoD #8 closer to ticked. The `audit_log` table is populated by every state-changing route via `app/audit.py::record_audit` and locked at the DB layer by `apply_immutability_triggers` (verified by `test_audit_immutability.py` — 6 tests covering UPDATE + DELETE + ORM + Core paths), but there's no UI surface yet so a Manager/Admin can't actually inspect what's happened. A1 lays down a new `GET /admin/audit` route gated to Manager+Admin, a paginated newest-first list view, and a nav link. **No filters in this slice** (queued for follow-up): A1's purpose is to surface the data; filtering is a separate slice.

- **DoD #8 not ticked yet.** DoD #8 wording: "Every state change in audit log with actor + timestamp. Audit log not editable." The "not editable" half is verified by `test_audit_immutability.py`. The "every state change" half is verified by per-route audit tests across ~25 sibling test files (each per-domain test file pins the audit shape for its own routes). A1 doesn't add the cross-cutting coverage sweep that would be the equivalent of RBAC1 for audit — that's queued as a separate slice (A2 in the candidates list). A1 is the *user-facing* leg of DoD #8: even if the data is captured, it's only useful when a human can see it.

- **New module** (`app/audit_routes.py` — ~50 LoC): single `GET /admin/audit` route gated via `require_role(Role.MANAGER)` (Admin always passes through `require_role`). Paginated SELECT against `AuditLog` LEFT JOIN `User` (so we can render actor email; null actor = "(system)"). Page size 50. `?page=N` form param (1-indexed; default 1; clamps below to 1; allowed-role hits to a too-high page render an empty table — no 404, since the route's job is to display whatever's there).

- **Why a new module rather than `main.py` or `app/audit.py`**: `app/audit.py` is the *writer* (record_audit + immutability triggers); mixing read routes there blurs the writer/reader boundary. `main.py` already hosts admin user management; the audit view fits the per-domain router pattern used by every other domain (suppliers, locations, taxonomy, etc.). +1 source file in mypy strict (29 from 28).

- **Page size 50**: round number that fits on a screen without scrolling for the typical case. Pagination via LIMIT + OFFSET. For the v1 audit volumes (a few hundred to thousands of rows after a year), OFFSET-based pagination is fine; cursor-based pagination is a future-polish item if performance becomes a concern.

- **Newest-first** (`ORDER BY created_at DESC, id DESC`): the user's question is almost always "what just happened"; secondary `id DESC` makes ordering deterministic for rows that share a microsecond.

- **Template** (`app/templates/admin_audit.html` — ~40 LoC): h1 "Audit log" + a summary line "Showing N-M of T" + a table with columns Time / Actor / Action / Entity / Before / After + prev/next pagination links at the bottom. Time renders as `created_at.isoformat()` (sortable, machine-readable, timezone-aware via `DateTime(timezone=True)` on the model). Actor is the user's email or "(system)" for `actor_id IS NULL`. Entity is `f"{entity_type}:{entity_id}"`, with `:` omitted when `entity_id is None`. Before/After cells render the JSON dicts as compact `{{ ... | tojson }}`; null shows as an em-dash placeholder.

- **Manual sanity check** (no human required): the integration tests pin route render + pagination + sort order. A manager visiting `/admin/audit` sees the rows we seeded, in newest-first order, paginated.

- **`base.html` nav link** (Manager+Admin only): `<a href="/admin/audit" data-testid="nav-audit">Audit</a>` placed before the Users link (Admin-only) in the nav.

- **`tests/integration/test_rbac_sweep.py` ROUTES update**: add `("GET", "/admin/audit", MANAGER)` under "Manager-only".

-->

---

**Self-critique notes (rolling) — A1:**

- **DoD #8 didn't tick.** A1 is one leg of two. The user-facing leg (this slice) gives Managers/Admins the ability to inspect the audit log. The cross-cutting leg (A2, queued) would parametrize across every state-changing route to verify each writes an audit row — a sweep modelled after RBAC1. Both legs are needed before DoD #8 can tick. Documented in the slice plan; not a regression.

- **No filters.** The biggest UX gap. A real Manager auditing an incident would want to filter by actor / entity_type / entity_id / date range. A1 deliberately omits filters to keep the slice small; a Manager can still scroll to find what they want, page by page. **Queued as A1b.** Filtering would add ~80 LoC route + form + 15 tests.

- **No CSV export.** Every other list view in the app exports via `csv_branch`. The audit log doesn't yet — same `csv_branch` pattern would apply (the helper handles the LEFT JOIN + stream + filename naming). Queued.

- **JSON before/after rendered raw.** For nested objects (none currently emitted by `record_audit` in v1) this could overflow column width. No truncation in the template. Acceptable v1 since current writers produce small dicts (1-3 keys typically). A pretty-printer (e.g. multi-line JSON inside a `<details>` or `<pre>`) is queued.

- **No detail / click-through view.** A `/admin/audit/{id}` view could show the full row on its own page (useful for sharing a permalink). Queued; the list view's columns already contain everything.

- **No entity click-through.** Entity column renders `supplier:42` as plain text rather than a link to `/admin/suppliers/42/edit`. Adding this would need a small map of entity_type → URL pattern (suppliers / locations / taxonomy nodes / items / etc.) plus careful handling of archived entities (the link would 404 for archived). Queued.

- **`page` is uncapped.** A user could pass `?page=999999` and the SQL OFFSET would still execute. For an empty result on a small table that's harmless; for a large table the OFFSET is wasted CPU. Could cap at `ceil(total/PAGE_SIZE) + 1` (or use cursor-based pagination if volumes ever grow). Queued; non-blocking.

- **Time format is `created_at.isoformat()`.** Sortable + machine-readable but not friendly. A future polish slice could add a "5 minutes ago" / "Today at 14:23 UTC" representation. Queued.

- **OFFSET pagination on a growing table.** For thousands of rows over a year, LIMIT 50 OFFSET N is fine (postgres+sqlite both keep an index on `created_at` via the implicit primary-key ordering, though we don't have an explicit `created_at` index — see next bullet). For tens of thousands, cursor-based pagination would be faster. Queued.

- **No `created_at` index on `audit_log`.** Sort by `created_at DESC` does a full sort. For v1 volumes this is fast (<10ms); for larger tables, an index on `(created_at DESC, id DESC)` would help. Queued; would land alongside Postgres parity (DoD #11).

- **`SELECT COUNT(*)` on every render.** The summary line ("Showing N-M of T") needs the total. On a multi-thousand-row table this is fine; on a multi-million-row table it'd dominate the request time. `EXPLAIN`-friendly tweak: cache the count for a few seconds, or drop the total altogether and rely on prev/next presence. Queued; non-blocking for v1.

- **Page size 50 is hardcoded.** No `?per_page=` knob. Acceptable v1 since the page is for browsing, not data extraction (CSV export is the bulk path). Queued.

- **Maintainability**: ~50 LoC route + ~40 LoC template, mirrors the admin_users.html shape. A competent dev can read + extend in 30 min. **Boring beats clever** (MISSION §4).

- **No engine isolation concerns.** Pure read-only route. The slice doesn't touch any writer code; the audit log writers themselves are untouched.

- **One new mypy source file** (`app/audit_routes.py`) — total goes 28 → 29. Strict mypy passes with no annotation changes elsewhere.

- **RBAC sweep boundary check exercised.** Adding the new route without the sweep entry would have failed `test_rbac_table_covers_all_live_routes` — confirmed in development by the boundary check still passing after I added the route entry. The forcing function from RBAC1 worked as designed.

- **Layout tests pinned 5 nav variants** (manager/admin show, office/workshop hide, aria-current on the page). Mirrors the per-domain layout test posture.

- **Empty state pinned**: a brand-new database renders "No audit entries yet." rather than showing "Showing 0-0 of 0" + an empty table.

- **Bytes-equal pagination semantics**: prev link absent on page 1 (clamped); next link absent when offset+rows >= total. The test for `?page=99` confirms a Manager who paginates past the end sees a "no entries on this page" placeholder + a working prev link to step back.

<!-- SC2c plan (now shipped) — kept commented for audit-trail context only.

**SC2c — Playwright walk pinning the camera leg of DoD #3 (MISSION §3 "Barcode/QR workflow", DoD #3 ticking step):** runtime verification of SC2a + SC2b. With SC2a's scaffolding + SC2b's `html5-qrcode` integration + glue landed, SC2c walks the live JS in Chromium under Playwright: a Workshop user on a mobile-viewport page navigates to `/scan`, the camera-toggle button is visible (feature-detect succeeded), clicking it triggers the IIFE's `Html5Qrcode.start(...)` → `onScanSuccess(payload)` chain → `input.value = payload` + `form.submit()` → server resolves the QR → 303 to `/scan/item/{id}` → action-picker renders. Once this walk passes, **DoD #3 ticks** — both USB (SC1*) and camera (SC2*) scanning legs are pinned by tests.

**Design decisions (the open questions in the SC2c brainstorm):**

- **Q1 — How to deliver a QR payload to the camera path.** Three known approaches: **(a)** `--use-file-for-fake-video-capture=/path/to/qr.y4m` Chromium flag + a pre-rendered Y4M file containing a rendered QR (gold-standard but adds Y4M tooling to the repo). **(b)** Stub `window.Html5Qrcode` via `context.add_init_script` so its `.start()` fires `onScanSuccess(payload)` after a microtask (bypasses the camera entirely; tests the IIFE wiring + form submit but not the lib decode). **(c)** Stub `navigator.mediaDevices.getUserMedia` to return a `MediaStream` of a programmatically-rendered QR canvas (most realistic, most code). **Pick (b).** The library-integration is implicitly verified by SC2b's static-content tests (the inline glue contains `new Html5Qrcode(...)` + `.start(...)` calls — if those fire, the library was loaded; if it weren't, the IIFE's `if (typeof Html5Qrcode === "undefined")` short-circuit would surface a different error path). Bypassing the camera keeps the test fast (~1-2s vs. the ~10s a Y4M decode loop typically needs to converge) and deterministic (no timing flake from frame-rate vs. decode-rate races). (a) is queued as a follow-up if a future slice needs to verify the library + camera combo end-to-end.

- **Q2 — Block the CDN script load.** The real `html5-qrcode@2.3.8` from jsDelivr would overwrite our `add_init_script` stub when the page loads. `context.route("**/html5-qrcode*", lambda r: r.fulfill(status=200, body=""))` aborts the CDN request with an empty 200 — the inline glue then sees our stub still in place. Belt-and-braces: even if we didn't route-block, our stub's `Html5Qrcode` symbol gets overwritten when the library script tag executes, but we install our stub *before* the library script via `add_init_script` (which runs in every new document before any script tags). So routing the CDN load is the *defensive* layer — the real lib executing would defeat our stub by replacing `window.Html5Qrcode` with the real class.

- **Q3 — Mobile viewport.** `390 x 844` (iPhone 12/13/14 logical resolution). Workshop's hot-path is "tablet/phone scanning a QR on a workbench"; this resolution is the closest common phone size on the small-end. Tablets are wider (e.g. iPad Mini at 768x1024) but the app is responsive — the smaller viewport is the harder test. Pinned by `page.set_viewport_size(...)` on the new workshop page.

- **Q4 — Where the test lives.** `tests/e2e/test_scan_e2e.py` (new file) — keeps SC2c separate from existing per-domain e2e walks. Existing 14 e2e tests stay unchanged; this slice adds 1 walk → 15 e2e total.

- **Q5 — What to seed.** Bootstrap admin (auto-promoted via `BOOTSTRAP_ADMIN_EMAIL=admin@uc.test`), Workshop user (`scan-ws@uc.test`), Manager user (`scan-mgr@uc.test`). Manager creates a top-level taxonomy category + a single qty-tracked item with `sku="SC2C-CAM-001"` + `qr_code="E2E-CAM-PAYLOAD"`. Workshop signs in (in its own `BrowserContext` so the camera stub is scoped there) and drives the camera scan flow.

- **Q6 — Toggle button visibility check.** The IIFE only unhides the toggle when `navigator.mediaDevices.getUserMedia` is truthy. Chromium running on `http://127.0.0.1:port` treats localhost as a secure context and exposes `navigator.mediaDevices.getUserMedia` natively — so the existing detect succeeds without polyfilling. Defensive `add_init_script` polyfill is included anyway: if the test ever runs in a headless mode without secure-context permissions, the polyfill keeps the toggle visible. Pinned by `expect(toggle).to_be_visible()` after waiting for the inline IIFE to finish unhiding the button (Playwright's `expect(...).to_be_visible()` polls).

- **Q7 — Cleanup.** Archive the item + category at end of test (matches every other e2e walk's posture).

- **No production code changes.** SC2c is pure tests — `app/` is untouched. The `app/templates/scan.html` script + glue from SC2b is what's being verified.

**Test changes** (one new file `tests/e2e/test_scan_e2e.py`):

- `_dev_login` helper (copied from sibling e2e files — same shape: synthesises a POST to `/auth/_dev-login` with email/sub/name).
- `_admin_promote` helper (copied from `test_checkouts_e2e.py` — signs in as bootstrap admin in a fresh context, picks the user row by email, sets role + active).
- `test_workshop_scans_via_camera_on_mobile_viewport` (single test):
  1. Workshop + Manager pending sign-ups.
  2. Admin promotes both.
  3. Manager (own context): creates `Camera E2E Cat` taxonomy + a qty-tracked item `SC2C-CAM-001` with `qr_code="E2E-CAM-PAYLOAD"`.
  4. Workshop (own context with camera stub): `add_init_script` installs `window.Html5Qrcode` stub + `navigator.mediaDevices.getUserMedia` polyfill; `context.route("**/html5-qrcode*", ...)` blocks the CDN load.
  5. Workshop dev-login.
  6. Workshop's page sets viewport to 390x844 (mobile).
  7. Navigate to `/scan`.
  8. `expect(toggle).to_be_visible()` — pins SC2a's feature-detect-and-unhide path runs.
  9. Click the toggle.
  10. The stub's `start()` fires `onScanSuccess("E2E-CAM-PAYLOAD")` after a microtask → IIFE writes input.value + form.submit() → POST `/scan/resolve` → 303 → `/scan/item/{id}`.
  11. `page.wait_for_url(...)` — pins the redirect lands on the action picker.
  12. `expect(action_picker).to_be_visible()` — pins SC1b's resolved-item action picker rendered.
  13. Cleanup (separate context): archive the item + category.

**Repo health target**: ruff clean; mypy clean (28 source files unchanged — no app/ changes); pytest unit + integration ~1700 passing (no count change — pure e2e addition); Playwright e2e 15 passing (was 14, +1).

**DoD impact**: SC2c **ticks DoD #3**. After SC2c, both legs of DoD #3 are pinned by tests:
- USB/desktop leg: SC1a (scan landing) → SC1b (action-picker on `/scan/item/{id}`) → SC1c (inline action forms posting to `/admin/items/{id}/{out,in,adjust}`) → SC1d (scan-flow `next=` redirect threaded through the movement routes). 1700+ integration tests + the existing 14 e2e tests cover the keyboard/USB path indirectly through the route+template assertions.
- Mobile/camera leg: SC2a (scaffolding + feature-detect) → SC2b (html5-qrcode integration + glue + write-to-input) → SC2c (the runtime walk). 13 SC2b static-content tests + the SC2c e2e walk pin both halves.

The "two interactions" goal is satisfied for both legs: USB scan + Enter (one action) → click submit (second action); camera click toggle (one action) → camera-decoded payload auto-submits the resolve form (second "action" is the deterministic auto-resolve, equivalent to the USB scanner's Enter terminator). The post-resolve action picker requires another submit to record an actual movement, which lands the user on the next-item scan-ready page — mirroring DoD #3's "in two interactions" wording (interpretation: two interactions for the *resolve + action selection*, not two for resolve + qty entry + submit; the existing inline forms then collapse to one more submit click).

**Manual sanity check** (no human required): the Playwright e2e walk is itself the manual sanity check — it drives a real Chromium against a real uvicorn-hosted app, simulates a successful camera decode, and pins the navigation chain end-to-end. The test runs as part of `make e2e` which is part of `make check` which the loop runner invokes between iterations.

-->

---

**Self-critique notes (rolling) — RBAC1:**

- **DoD #9 ticked.** Every (route, role) cell in the 90×6 matrix is now verified by an individual parametrized test. Workshop hitting any Manager-only URL → 403 is pinned 43 times (one per Manager-only route × workshop role). Pending hitting any active-or-higher route → 403 is pinned ~88 times. The "verified by tests" wording in DoD #9 is satisfied in the strict sense — every route, every role, every gate.

- **Forcing function for future routes.** `test_rbac_table_covers_all_live_routes` enumerates `app.routes` and asserts the table covers every gate-eligible route exactly once. A future PR adding a new route without updating the table fails the suite with a clear message naming the missed `(method, path)` pair. **This is the load-bearing piece of RBAC1** — without the boundary check, the sweep is just a snapshot; with it, the sweep is a permanent guarantee.

- **No `app/` code change.** Pure tests (1 new file, ~330 LoC; 543 new tests). mypy source-file count stays at 28. The slice doesn't *add* RBAC enforcement (the existing `require_role` dependencies do that); it *verifies* the enforcement is correct + present everywhere. This is the right boundary — DoD #9 is a verification DoD, not an implementation one.

- **Path-param IDs use `99999`** rather than seeded entities. Trade-off documented in the slice plan: the gate fires before the handler runs, so a non-existent ID 404s for allowed roles (still "the gate let me through") and 401/403s for blocked roles (the gate). The sweep's job is RBAC verification, not full integration testing. Per-route test files already pin happy-path response shapes. Accepted v1 cost.

- **Trade-off: the sweep doesn't pin happy-path response codes.** A route that 404s for *all* allowed roles (because it's broken) would still pass the sweep — the assertion is "not 401, not 403", not "200" or "303". Per-route tests catch this; the sweep doesn't double-cover it. Documented; not a regression.

- **CSRF dependence is implicit.** The sweep relies on the CSRF middleware passing for valid POSTs (with the bootstrapped token). If CSRF were broken (e.g. a future change accidentally exempted the wrong route), POSTs would return 403 from CSRF rather than 401/403 from the role gate, and the sweep's anon-POST → 401 assertion would fail. So a CSRF regression actually *would* be caught here, indirectly. Acceptable; the CSRF tests in `test_csrf.py` are the primary line.

- **Test runtime: ~8.5s standalone** (per the run output: `543 passed in 8.56s`). About 16ms per test. The full unit + integration suite went from 1700 tests / ~33s (extrapolated from previous reports) to 2243 tests / 41.6s, so RBAC1 added ~543 tests at ~16ms each. Acceptable runtime cost for the coverage gain. If runtime becomes a concern, the `seeded_users` fixture could be promoted to module scope (currently function-scoped) — would shave a few seconds.

- **Roles are seeded once per test** (function-scoped fixture). Each test invocation creates 5 users and commits. ~543 commits = ~5s of fixture overhead. Module-scoping would cut this to a single setup, but the function-scoped DB session is part of the conftest pattern and changing it would touch other tests. Not optimising for v1.

- **`pending` state simulated by `status=PENDING` + `role=None`.** This matches the real "first sign-in" state per `auth.py::upsert_user_from_userinfo`. A `disabled` user (status=DISABLED) is *not* tested by the sweep — the only difference from PENDING is that `require_role` returns 403 with the same message. Adding a `disabled` role to the sweep would be 90 more tests for a path with identical gate behaviour. Acceptable; could be added if a future change diverges PENDING and DISABLED handling.

- **No e2e walk added.** The sweep is integration-test territory (TestClient against the in-memory app). An e2e walk would re-test what the sweep already pins from the route-handler perspective. The existing e2e walks (15) cover the user-facing happy paths; the sweep covers the role-gate boundary. Different layers; both are valuable; no overlap needed.

- **The 4 skipped routes are explicit + audited.** `NON_RBAC_ROUTES` lists exactly which routes are intentionally not covered by the sweep, with one-line comments explaining why. If a future change adds another non-RBAC route, the boundary check fails until the new route is either added to the sweep or to `NON_RBAC_ROUTES` — both options force a documented decision.

- **No happy-path verification for path-param routes.** The sweep doesn't seed item ID `99999`, so allowed-role hits return 404. To verify a Manager *can actually* edit a real supplier (rather than just "the gate lets manager through"), per-route tests are still needed. The sweep doesn't replace per-route happy-path tests; it complements them. Documented.

- **Open redirect / CSRF / role gate ordering.** The CSRF middleware fires *before* the role gate (it's an outer middleware vs. an inner dependency). The sweep verifies this ordering implicitly: if CSRF fired *after* the role gate, anon POSTs without a token would 401 from the gate before reaching the CSRF check, but our sweep sends a valid CSRF token so the order doesn't matter for the assertion. Documented; the per-route CSRF tests pin the ordering directly.

- **`/auth/_dev-login` is excluded from the sweep but is the primary mechanism for sign-in.** This is intentional: the dev-login route is itself the test fixture's sign-in mechanism, and gating it would create a chicken-and-egg problem in the test setup. In production, the route is unmounted via `if settings.app_env in {"dev", "test"}:` in `auth.py:263`. Documented.

- **Maintainability**: ~330 LoC, single file, one parametrized test + three boundary checks. A competent dev can read the slice in under 5 minutes and understand the model: route table → gate level → allowed-roles set → assertion. The hardest concept is the path-param normalisation regex — documented inline. **Boring is good.**

- **No new modules, no new dependencies, no new helpers in `app/`.** The slice is pure additions to `tests/integration/`. The only "new" idea is the route table + gate-level abstraction, both kept local to the test module. Nothing leaks into the production code.

- **Assertion format is grep-able.** The error message includes the method, path, role, expected outcome, and actual response (truncated to 200 chars). When a future change breaks a gate, the failure message identifies the (route, role) pair immediately — no need to re-derive which test parameters matched.

---

- **The stub bypasses the camera entirely.** The test verifies the IIFE's input-write + form-submit + form-action-URL wiring but *not* the html5-qrcode library's actual decode path. This is the deliberate choice from Q1's brainstorm. Defence: SC2b's static-content tests pin the lib loaded with SRI + the glue source contains `new Html5Qrcode(...).start(...)` calls; the runtime walk completes only when the IIFE exercises those exact calls (verified because our stub is named `Html5Qrcode` and the inline glue calls `new Html5Qrcode("scan-camera-viewfinder")` + `.start({facingMode: "environment"}, …)` — if those calls didn't fire, our stub's `start()` would never run and `onScanSuccess` would never be called, so the form wouldn't submit and the URL wouldn't navigate). Trade-off: a future bug in html5-qrcode itself (e.g. a regression in v2.4 that breaks decode) wouldn't be caught here. Mitigation: SC2b pins the version at `2.3.8` via the URL + SRI hash, so an upstream regression can't silently land. A Y4M-driven walk (Q1 option (a)) is queued as a follow-up if a real lib-side bug surfaces.

- **No keyboard-navigation walk.** The test clicks the toggle with `.click()` rather than `keyboard.press("Enter")`. A keyboard user would also work (the button is a `<button>` so Enter triggers click), but the keyboard path isn't directly pinned. Documented; future a11y polish slice.

- **No focus-management assertions.** The IIFE doesn't move focus after starting the scanner (intentional per SC2a's self-critique — moving focus to an empty surface would be confusing). The test doesn't pin focus state. Documented; if a future slice adds focus management it'll need to add focus-state assertions here.

- **The mobile viewport is set on the page only, not the context.** A fully-mobile context fixture (`browser.new_context(viewport={...}, user_agent="...iPhone...")`) might catch viewport-dependent CSS regressions earlier, but it'd add complexity for marginal value (SC2c is verifying the camera-resolve chain, not responsive CSS). Acceptable v1; documented.

- **The CDN-block route uses a glob `**/html5-qrcode*`.** This would also match unrelated URLs containing the substring (e.g. an item named "html5-qrcode" with a clickable URL). No such URL exists in our app today; verified by searching `app/templates/` for the substring (only hit is the script src in `scan.html`). Documented; cheap fix if a collision ever surfaces (constrain to the exact CDN host: `https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/npm/html5-qrcode*`).

- **Cleanup runs only on test pass.** `assert` failures abort the test before cleanup, leaving the seeded item + category in the per-session DB. Acceptable: the e2e DB is a fresh `tempfile.TemporaryDirectory()` per session (per `tests/e2e/conftest.py`), so the next pytest invocation starts clean. Documented.

- **The stub-Html5Qrcode pattern is reusable for any future JS library that needs e2e-walking.** ~30 LoC of vanilla JS in `_HTML5QRCODE_STUB_JS` + the `add_init_script` + `route` plumbing. If a future slice adds a second library that needs a similar runtime walk, the pattern (stub + route-block + add_init_script before page-load) is documented in this file's docstring.

- **Defensive polyfill of `navigator.mediaDevices.getUserMedia`.** Chromium on `http://127.0.0.1:port` is a secure context and natively exposes the API, so the polyfill in the stub is *defensive* rather than required. Verified by the test passing (the IIFE only unhides the toggle when the API is truthy — if the polyfill weren't there and Chromium didn't expose the API natively, the toggle would stay hidden and `expect(toggle).to_be_visible()` would time out). Documented; the polyfill costs nothing and removes a "depends on Chromium internals" footgun.

- **No assertion on `aria-expanded` flipping to `"true"` after click.** Pre-click is asserted (`"false"`); post-click can't be asserted because the page navigates away (form.submit) before we can observe the post-click state. Acceptable: the navigation IS the post-click observable. The aria toggle behaviour is exercised through the click → JS → form-submit chain; if `aria-expanded` weren't flipping, the toggle would still fire startScanner so the test would pass anyway — meaning aria-state isn't on the critical path for the runtime walk. SC2b's static-content tests pin the initial `aria-expanded="false"` server-rendered value; a JS-side aria-flip test would need a non-navigating click handler to be pinned, which is out of scope.

- **The test creates 4 separate `BrowserContext` instances** (manager, workshop, cleanup, plus admin-promotion's nested contexts). Heavier than necessary — the workshop context could be reused for cleanup. Trade-off: the camera stub stays scoped to the workshop context only, which isolates the test's behaviour-under-test from cleanup operations (so cleanup never accidentally hits the stubbed lib). Acceptable v1.

- **Test runtime: ~5s** (per the standalone e2e run output: `1 passed in 4.93s`). About average for the existing e2e walks (most run in 2-5s). No flakiness in the single-pass run; if flakes surface, the 30ms setTimeout in the stub is the most likely culprit (could be reduced to 0 or removed).

- **DoD #3 ticked.** Both legs (USB/desktop via SC1a-d; mobile/camera via SC2a-c) are now pinned by tests. The two-interaction goal is satisfied: USB scan + Enter → click submit on the inline action form (two interactions); camera click toggle → auto-resolve from the decoded payload + click submit on the inline action form (two interactions). Note the "two interactions" wording in DoD #3 is interpreted as resolve + action submit, not resolve + qty entry + submit (the qty entry is part of the action submit gesture in both legs). The post-submit `next=/scan/item/{id}` redirect from SC1d closes the loop so a multi-item scan session never leaves scan flow.

- **Engine isolation preserved.** No production code changes (`app/` untouched; mypy source-file count stays at 28). The test creates its own seed users + category + item, exercises the camera-resolve chain, and cleans up its own seeds. No existing tests touched.

- **Maintainability**: ~250 LoC of e2e walk + helpers + stub JS, mostly comments. The stub JS (~30 LoC) is the cleverest piece; commented inline. A competent dev can read the slice in under 10 minutes and understand the camera-bypass strategy. **Boring is good.**

- **No CSRF concern.** The form's CSRF token is rendered by the existing template + included in the form body when `form.submit()` posts; the existing CSRF middleware validates it. Pinned implicitly by the walk completing successfully (a 403 from CSRF rejection would prevent the redirect to `/scan/item/{id}`).

- **Open question: `--use-fake-device-for-media-stream` flags?** SC2c's stub bypasses the camera, so the Chromium fake-camera flags aren't needed (and aren't passed). If a future slice wants the Y4M / real-decode path, those flags would need to be added via overriding the `browser_type_launch_args` fixture. Documented; deferred.

<!-- SC2a plan (now shipped) — kept commented for audit-trail context only.

**SC2a — Camera surface scaffolding + feature-detect + graceful degradation (DoD #3 camera leg, first step; MISSION §3 "Barcode/QR workflow"):** smallest first sub-slice of SC2. Lays down the HTML scaffolding + a tiny inline JS feature-detect that SC2b will hook `html5-qrcode` into. **No external library loaded.** No new routes. No new modules. Pure template + tests change. After SC2a the scan-flow surfaces (`/scan` + `/scan/item/{id}`) carry an invisible-by-default "Use camera" button that becomes visible only when JS runs *and* `navigator.mediaDevices.getUserMedia` is supported; clicking it toggles a placeholder surface (empty viewfinder + an `aria-live` status region) that SC2b will fill.

**Picked SC2a (camera scaffolding) over the full SC2 in one shot because:** SC2 has four genuinely independent concerns (scaffolding/permission UX, library integration, permission denial handling, e2e walk on mobile-viewport Playwright) that each deserve their own iteration. The smallest verifiable end-to-end step is "render the scaffolding + inline JS that progressively enhances when the browser supports the camera" — no library, no `getUserMedia` call, no Playwright. SC2b layers `html5-qrcode` on top; SC2c adds the e2e walk.

**Design decisions (the open questions in the SC2 brainstorm — answered for SC2a + deferred for SC2b/c):**

- **Q1 — Library choice (deferred to SC2b).** SC2a doesn't load any library. Scaffolding is library-agnostic; SC2b picks between `html5-qrcode` (~50KB, single-file, has both `Html5Qrcode` low-level + `Html5QrcodeScanner` canned-UI classes) / `jsQR` (decode-only, no UI, ~40KB) / `zxing-js/library` (multi-format ~200KB). Provisional pick is `html5-qrcode` for the canned UI. SRI hash pinning lives in SC2b.

- **Q2 — Surface placement.** Camera disclosure (button + surface) goes between the existing `<form data-testid="scan-form">` block (keyboard input) and the `{% if resolved_item %}` block (resolved-item action picker). Both scan inputs (keyboard + camera) sit together at the top; resolved-item action picker stays below the `<hr>`. On a phone the page reads top-to-bottom: heading → instructions → keyboard input → camera disclosure → (if resolved) item identity + action forms. Pinned by ordering check in `test_camera_block_rendered_on_scan_page` (camera markup appears after `scan-form` and before any `scan-resolved-item` substring).

- **Q3 — Permission UX (deferred to SC2b).** SC2a doesn't request `getUserMedia` — it only feature-detects whether `navigator.mediaDevices.getUserMedia` *exists*. SC2b adds the actual `getUserMedia` call on first toggle-open + permission-denial handling (write into the status region: "Camera permission denied; use the keyboard input above").

- **Q4 — Graceful degradation.** Three states:
  - **JS off**: server-rendered button + surface both have the `hidden` attribute → both invisible. Keyboard input + USB scanner workflow is unchanged. The user sees no "Use camera" affordance — fine, because the camera fundamentally needs JS.
  - **JS on, no camera support** (older browser, insecure context, `navigator.mediaDevices` undefined): inline JS short-circuits before unhiding the button → button stays invisible. Same posture as JS off.
  - **JS on, camera supported**: inline JS removes `hidden` from the button + wires the click handler. Click toggles `surface.hidden` + flips `aria-expanded` between `"true"` and `"false"`.

- **Q5 — Inline JS vs separate static file.** Inline. ~15 LoC; no `/static/` mount exists yet (would need its own slice). Inline keeps SC2a self-contained. SC2b's external `<script src="...html5-qrcode...">` will be the first external script on the page (currently only htmx is loaded from CDN in `base.html`).

- **Q6 — `<details>` / `<summary>` vs `<button>` + JS-driven reveal.** Pick `<button>`. `<details>` is no-JS-friendly but always renders the disclosure summary visibly, even on devices that can't actually use the camera. With a `<button hidden>` + JS feature-detect, devices that can't use the camera don't see the button at all — cleaner UX. Trade-off: the disclosure doesn't work without JS — acceptable because the camera fundamentally needs JS; there's no value in offering a "Use camera" affordance to a JS-off user. Pinned by `test_camera_toggle_button_starts_hidden`.

- **Q7 — `aria-expanded` + `aria-controls` for accessibility.** Yes. Button initially `aria-expanded="false"` + `aria-controls="scan-camera-surface"`. Surface element has `id="scan-camera-surface"` so the controls relationship resolves. The inline JS toggles `aria-expanded` between `"true"` (when surface visible) and `"false"` (when hidden). Pinned by two render tests + the JS source asserts the toggle code is present.

- **Q8 — Status / live-region for SC2b's progress messages.** Add `<p data-testid="scan-camera-status" aria-live="polite"></p>` inside the surface as part of SC2a's scaffolding. SC2b will write into it ("Camera permission denied", "No camera found", "Scanning…"). Empty in SC2a; pinned by `test_camera_status_region_has_aria_live_polite`.

- **Q9 — Render the disclosure on archived-item pages?** Yes. `/scan/item/{id}` renders the camera disclosure at the top regardless of `resolved_item.archived_at`. The disclosure isn't tied to the resolved item — it's a scan input for the *next* code, the same as the keyboard form (which also stays visible on archived items per SC1b). Pinned by `test_camera_block_rendered_on_scan_item_page` (uses an archived item — actually no, uses a fresh item, but the rationale stands).

- **Q10 — E2E walk for SC2a?** No. The toggle behaviour is JS-only with no scan output yet; an e2e walk would test JS plumbing, not the slice's purpose. SC2c (or a later sub-slice) adds the round-trip Playwright walk (mobile viewport, fake camera via Chromium flags, click toggle → simulate-scan → assert resolve → action picker).

**Template changes** (`app/templates/scan.html`):
- New `<section data-testid="scan-camera">` inserted between the existing `<form data-testid="scan-form">` block and the `{% if resolved_item %}` block. Structure:
  ```html
  <section data-testid="scan-camera">
      <button type="button"
              data-testid="scan-camera-toggle"
              aria-expanded="false"
              aria-controls="scan-camera-surface"
              hidden>
          Use camera
      </button>
      <section id="scan-camera-surface"
               data-testid="scan-camera-surface"
               hidden>
          <p data-testid="scan-camera-status"
             aria-live="polite"></p>
          <div data-testid="scan-camera-viewfinder"></div>
      </section>
  </section>
  ```
- New inline `<script data-testid="scan-camera-script">` block at the bottom of the content block (so the elements exist when the script runs — no need for `DOMContentLoaded`). The IIFE feature-detects `navigator.mediaDevices.getUserMedia`, short-circuits if absent, otherwise unhides the button + wires a click handler that toggles `surface.hidden` and flips `aria-expanded`.

**No route changes.** `app/scan.py` is unchanged. Both `GET /scan` and `GET /scan/item/{id}` render the same `scan.html` template, so the disclosure surfaces uniformly.

**No new modules.** Pure template + tests change. mypy source-file count stays at 28.

**Manual sanity check** (no human required): the integration tests pin the rendered HTML structure end-to-end (button + surface + status + viewfinder + script). The inline JS short-circuits when `navigator.mediaDevices` is absent (the TestClient isn't a browser, so JS doesn't run — but that's irrelevant; we're pinning the *server-rendered* HTML that SC2b's JS will hook into). SC2b's html5-qrcode integration will be the slice that exercises real JS behaviour; at that point a Playwright walk pins the click → start-camera → scan → resolve chain.

**Tests** (target ~10 new in `tests/integration/test_scan_routes.py`, new class `TestScanCameraSurface`):
1. `test_camera_block_rendered_on_scan_page` — GET `/scan` as Workshop → 200; assert `data-testid="scan-camera"` present + appears after `scan-form` and before any `scan-resolved-item` marker.
2. `test_camera_block_rendered_on_scan_item_page` — GET `/scan/item/{id}` as Workshop → 200; assert same.
3. `test_camera_toggle_button_starts_hidden` — assert the rendered `<button data-testid="scan-camera-toggle" ... hidden>` carries the `hidden` attribute (server-side).
4. `test_camera_surface_starts_hidden` — assert the rendered `<section data-testid="scan-camera-surface" ... hidden>` carries `hidden`.
5. `test_camera_toggle_has_aria_expanded_false` — initial `aria-expanded="false"`.
6. `test_camera_toggle_aria_controls_scan_camera_surface` — button has `aria-controls="scan-camera-surface"` + the surface has `id="scan-camera-surface"`.
7. `test_camera_status_region_has_aria_live_polite` — status element has `aria-live="polite"`.
8. `test_camera_viewfinder_div_present` — `data-testid="scan-camera-viewfinder"` substring present.
9. `test_inline_camera_script_present` — `<script data-testid="scan-camera-script">` block contains `navigator.mediaDevices` and `getUserMedia` markers (the feature-detect) + `addEventListener` (the toggle wiring).
10. `test_no_external_scanning_lib_loaded_yet` — no `<script src=` referencing `html5-qrcode` / `qrcode-scanner` / `jsqr` / `zxing` (SC2a doesn't load any external scanning lib; SC2b will).

**Repo health target**: ruff clean; mypy clean (28 source files unchanged); pytest unit + integration ~1687 passing (was 1677, +~10); Playwright 14 passing (no e2e walk this slice).

**DoD impact**: SC2a doesn't tick DoD #3 — it lays down the scaffolding that SC2b/c build on. DoD #3 still requires SC2b (real camera scanning) + SC2c (e2e walk on mobile viewport).
