<!-- SC1d plan (now shipped) — kept commented for audit-trail context only.

**SC1d — Thread `next=` redirect param through stock-in/out/adjust routes (DoD #3 desktop/USB leg polish, MISSION §3 "Barcode/QR workflow").** Continues SC1c. After SC1c a Workshop user can scan an item and submit an inline action form in two interactions, but the success redirect lands them on the per-action form (`/admin/items/{id}/{in,out,adjust}`) — to scan the next item they have to manually click `nav-scan`. SC1d threads an optional `next` form param through the three movement POST routes so scan-flow submits redirect back into scan flow (`/scan/item/{id}` — same item, with the post-mutation `current_qty` visible + the autofocused scan input ready for the next code).

DoD #3 wording is "record an in, out, or adjustment movement in two interactions" — SC1c already satisfies that for a single movement. SC1d makes a *multi-item* scan session viable (no manual nav-clicks between items) without adding to the per-movement interaction count. **DoD #3 still does not tick** — the camera leg (SC2) is required.

**Picked SC1d over SC2 (queued primary in Next slice) because:** (a) SC2 has open design questions (JS lib choice, surface placement, permission UX, graceful degradation) that genuinely deserve dedicated brainstorming + a fresh iteration — rushing it risks a bad library choice or a half-working camera surface; (b) SC1d is small (~25 LoC + ~12 tests) and is a natural continuation of SC1c — same files (`app/movements.py` + `app/templates/scan.html`); (c) shipping SC1d first means SC2's brainstorming has the *post-SC1d* scan flow as the baseline (scan-flow loop is round-trip-clean), which is a cleaner reference point than the current "land on per-action form" behaviour. SC2 is queued first in the Next slice for iteration 51, with brainstorming-before-coding.

**Design decisions (the four open questions in the SC1d brainstorm):**

- **Q1 — Where to redirect on success: same item (`/scan/item/{id}`) vs scan landing (`/scan`)?** Pick **same item**. Rationale: lands the user back on the scan-flow surface that shows the post-mutation `current_qty` (so they can verify what they just did), and the autofocused scan input on that page lets the next scan immediately resolve to a different item. Going to `/scan` would lose the "see what you did" feedback. Going to `/scan/item/{id}` is what the inline forms already advertise (the form actions point to `/admin/items/{id}/...`, so the user's mental model is "I'm acting on this item"); landing back on the scan-flow page for that item closes the loop visually.

- **Q2 — Whitelist policy for the `next` param (open-redirect prevention).** Allow exactly `path == "/scan"` or `path.startswith("/scan/")`. Rationale: covers the two scan-flow URLs we own (`/scan` + `/scan/item/{id}`); rejects `//evil.com/x` (doesn't match either pattern); rejects `/scanner/...` (close prefix but not a scan-flow URL); rejects every other path (`/admin/...`, etc.). A small private helper `_safe_scan_next(raw: str) -> str | None` returns the path if safe, `None` otherwise. The route call site is `target_url = _safe_scan_next(next_) or f"/admin/items/{item.id}/<action>"`. **Why not a URL parser**: Python's `urllib.parse.urlsplit` would parse `//evil.com/x` as `(scheme='', netloc='evil.com', path='/x')` — netloc-aware checks add complexity for marginal value. The two-prefix check is simpler and pinned by an explicit no-`//evil.com` test.

- **Q3 — Error-path behaviour: re-render with `next` preserved or drop it?** Drop it. Rationale: the two error paths (insufficient stock on `out` and `adjust direction=decrease`) re-render the per-action form template (`stock_out_form.html` / `stock_adjust_form.html`) with form values + an error block. Threading `next` through to the re-render would require (a) the helper `_render_stock_*_form` to accept `next_` and pass it into the template context, (b) the template to render a hidden `next` input, (c) tests pinning the round-trip. That's ~10-15 LoC + 2-3 tests across two templates for a rare path. Drop it instead: when a Workshop user hits insufficient-stock from scan flow, they land on the per-action form with the error and the full context (open value, recent movements). They've left scan flow, but they can use the bigger surface to recover and then nav back via `nav-scan`. The validation 400s (empty qty etc.) raise `HTTPException` directly with no body, so there's nothing to preserve there either. Documented in self-critique. Acceptable v1 cost.

- **Q4 — Should the per-action form (non-scan caller) also expose `next`?** No render-side change. The route accepts `next: str = Form("")` from any source; the per-action form templates (`stock_in_form.html` / `stock_out_form.html` / `stock_adjust_form.html`) don't render a hidden `next` input (would always be empty). Only `scan.html` renders the hidden input. Simplest impl; matches the "no per-action form template changes" boundary.

- **Route changes** (`app/movements.py`):
  - **New private helper** `_safe_scan_next(raw: str) -> str | None` placed near the other parse helpers (after `_parse_direction`, before `_get_item_or_404`). Returns the trimmed value if it equals `"/scan"` or starts with `"/scan/"`, else `None`. ~5 LoC.
  - **`record_stock_in` / `record_stock_out` / `record_stock_adjustment` (3 POST routes):** add `next_: str = Form("", alias="next")` form param (alias lets the form name stay `next` while the Python identifier avoids the builtin shadow + is visually distinct from the `Next slice` etc.; same `format_value` posture as the CSV branches). Replace the hardcoded `RedirectResponse(url=f"/admin/items/{item.id}/<action>", ...)` on each success path with `target_url = _safe_scan_next(next_) or f"/admin/items/{item.id}/<action>"; return RedirectResponse(url=target_url, ...)`. ~3 LoC per route. The flash (`_flash(request, ...)`) is unchanged — the flash region in `base.html` is shared across all surfaces, so the message surfaces on `/scan/item/{id}` automatically.
  - **No template changes** to `stock_in_form.html` / `stock_out_form.html` / `stock_adjust_form.html`. The error paths in `out` and `adjust direction=decrease` continue to re-render via `_render_stock_out_form` / `_render_stock_adjust_form` exactly as today (no `next` threading on the error path per Q3 decision).

- **Template changes** (`app/templates/scan.html`):
  - One hidden input added to each of the three inline forms: `<input type="hidden" name="next" value="/scan/item/{{ resolved_item.id }}">`. Placed right after the existing `csrf_token` hidden input on each form. 1 LoC × 3 = 3 LoC. The form action URLs and visible inputs are unchanged.

- **Tests** (target ~14 new in `tests/integration/test_movements_routes.py` + ~3 new in `tests/integration/test_scan_routes.py`):
  - In `test_movements_routes.py`:
    - `TestStockInNextRedirect` (4): no `next` → `/admin/items/{id}/in` (regression); `next=/scan/item/{id}` → that path; `next=/scan` → `/scan`; `next=/admin/items/X/in` → falls back to default; `next=//evil.com/x` → falls back to default.
    - `TestStockOutNextRedirect` (4): same shape — no `next`, `next=/scan/item/{id}`, `next=/scan`, `next=//evil.com/x`.
    - `TestStockAdjustNextRedirect` (4): same shape with `direction=increase` for the happy path; one extra test that on the *insufficient-stock* error path with `direction=decrease`, `next` is dropped (re-renders the per-action form, not a scan-flow redirect — pins Q3).
    - Total: 12-14 new tests across the three classes.
  - In `test_scan_routes.py`:
    - `TestScanItemPageInlineFormFields` extended with one assertion per form (3 tests or 1 test asserting all three) that the rendered `scan.html` carries `<input type="hidden" name="next" value="/scan/item/{id}">` inside each of `scan-out-form` / `scan-in-form` / `scan-adjust-form`. Pinned by checking the rendered HTML for the literal substring or by attribute lookup.
  - **Engine isolation preserved**: the existing `TestStockInHappyPath` / `TestStockOutHappyPath` / `TestStockAdjustIncrease/DecreaseHappyPath` tests don't pass a `next` param — they continue to assert the default redirect target. The new redirect tests are additive; no existing test reshape needed.

- **Manual sanity check** (no human required): `TestStockInNextRedirect::test_next_to_scan_item_redirects_to_scan_flow` posts a stock-in with `next=/scan/item/{id}` and asserts the 303 `Location` header is `/scan/item/{id}`. Combined with the existing happy-path tests pinning the cost layer + audit + current_qty bump, the chain is exercised: form posts → engine writes the layer + audit → flash is set → redirect lands on scan flow.

- **Repo health target**: ruff clean; mypy clean (28 source files unchanged — pure additions to `app/movements.py`, no new module); pytest unit + integration ~1675 passing (was 1661, +~14); Playwright 14 passing (no e2e walk added — same posture as SC1c; an e2e walk for the round-trip scan-flow chain is a candidate once SC2 lands and the camera surface adds e2e-only behaviour worth covering).

- **DoD impact**: SC1d does not tick a DoD on its own — it polishes DoD #3's desktop/USB leg (already substantively delivered by SC1c). DoD #3 still requires the camera leg (SC2) to tick.

-->

---

**Self-critique notes (rolling) — SC2a:**

- **DoD #3 still doesn't tick.** SC2a is scaffolding only — no library loaded, no `getUserMedia` call, no scan output. A user clicking the "Use camera" button on a JS+camera-capable device sees an empty surface (placeholder viewfinder + empty status region). Until SC2b lands the real scan path, this is a "preview" affordance with no value to a real user. Mitigation: SC2a + SC2b + SC2c are intended to ship as a coordinated trio; the slice plan and the Next-slice queue both pin SC2b as the immediate next iteration so the SC2a-only "click does nothing visible" state doesn't persist.
- **Empty surface on toggle-open is a UX dead-end pre-SC2b.** The status region is empty in SC2a. SC2b will write into it ("Camera permission denied" / "Scanning…" / "No camera found"). For SC2a's snapshot of behaviour, a curious user who clicks the button sees nothing happen visually except the surface revealing itself. Acceptable v1 cost because the button is feature-detected — only devices with `getUserMedia` see it at all, and SC2b should land in the same release window.
- **Inline `<script>` block bypasses any future CSP.** No Content Security Policy is currently configured in the app (verified — no `script-src` / `Content-Security-Policy` middleware anywhere in `app/`). If a future slice adds CSP with `script-src 'self'`, the inline block would break. SC2b will load an external CDN script for html5-qrcode — at that point the inline + external mix is the right time to think about CSP (likely pin a `'sha256-...'` hash for the inline block + `'self'` + `https://unpkg.com` for the externals). Documented; deferred.
- **No `<noscript>` fallback message added.** A user with JS off gets no explicit "camera unavailable" message. Trade-off: the keyboard input above is still fully functional, the camera is an *enhancement* not a fallback, and a `<noscript>` would just say "camera needs JavaScript" — redundant with the existing keyboard form. Documented; not a regression (camera surface is invisible without JS, same as if it didn't exist).
- **Feature-detect only checks `navigator.mediaDevices.getUserMedia` truthiness — not secure-context (HTTPS).** `getUserMedia` requires a secure context (HTTPS or `localhost`) on most browsers; calling it on `http://` non-localhost throws. SC2a's detect doesn't catch that case — it's only a "does the API exist" check. SC2b will discover the secure-context requirement at first call (the `getUserMedia` Promise rejects); the catch block will surface the message in the status region. Adding a secure-context check now (`window.isSecureContext` is the modern API) would be a 1-line addition, but without an actual `getUserMedia` call the check has no path to surface the message. Defer to SC2b. Documented.
- **Click handler doesn't move focus to the surface on toggle-open.** A keyboard / screen-reader user clicking "Use camera" hears `aria-expanded` flip from `"false"` to `"true"` but focus stays on the button. SC2b's start-camera flow will likely move focus to the status region (or announce the camera-started message via `aria-live`). For SC2a's no-op-on-click behaviour, leaving focus on the button is the right default — moving focus to an empty surface would be confusing. Pinned implicitly by the absence of any `.focus()` call in the inline JS.
- **Toggle button label is a generic "Use camera" — not "Scan with camera" or "Open camera scanner".** SC2b can refine the wording. The current label reads correctly with `aria-expanded` ("Use camera, button, expanded false"). Documented; flagged as a bikeshed-able copy decision for the SC2 brainstorm.
- **`hidden` attribute hides via the user-agent default `display: none` — no project CSS for it.** Modern browsers all honour the `hidden` attribute; very old browsers without UA `display: none` for `hidden` would render the toggle + surface unstyled. Negligible v1 concern (no IE support claimed). Acceptable.
- **The inline JS is server-rendered (and therefore *cached* by the browser as part of the HTML).** When SC2b lands and modifies the script, the cached HTML on a returning user's browser will still carry the SC2a-flavoured script for one request cycle. Acceptable — no breaking change between SC2a and SC2b's expected JS shape (SC2b's script extends the SC2a feature-detect; SC2a's IIFE is a no-op on completion).
- **Camera disclosure renders on archived-item pages too.** A user landing on `/scan/item/{archived-id}` sees the "Use camera" button (when JS+camera supported). The disclosure isn't tied to the resolved item — it's a scan input for the *next* code, same posture as the keyboard input form (which also stays visible on archived items per SC1b). Documented; pinned indirectly by `test_camera_block_rendered_on_scan_item_page` (uses a non-archived item, but the template branch isn't gated on `archived_at`).
- **Engine isolation preserved.** No routes change; no new modules; no new helpers. Source-file count stays at 28 (`mypy app` green). The existing tests all pass unchanged — the template extension is purely additive; the `data-testid="scan-camera-*"` markers don't collide with any existing test-ids (verified by searching `tests/` for `scan-camera` matches before this slice — zero hits).
- **No e2e walk added.** Same posture as SC1d. The toggle behaviour is JS-only with no scan output; an e2e walk that drove the click and asserted the surface revealed would test JS plumbing, not the slice's purpose. SC2c is the right place for the round-trip walk on a mobile-viewport Playwright run with a fake camera (`--use-fake-device-for-media-stream` + `--use-fake-ui-for-media-stream` Chromium flags); at that point there's a unique full-flow story (click toggle → start camera → simulate-scan → resolve → action picker) worth pinning end-to-end.
- **Maintainability**: ~24 LoC of HTML + ~15 LoC of inline JS in `app/templates/scan.html`. Vanilla browser APIs, no framework. The IIFE pattern is the standard one for "feature-detect + progressively enhance"; a competent dev can read the slice in under 5 minutes. **Boring is good.**
- **No CSRF concern.** No POSTs added; the camera disclosure is pure client-side reveal. `getUserMedia` (SC2b) is also client-side — no network call. The first network call from the camera path lands when the JS lib resolves a QR and submits the existing `/scan/resolve` form (which already has CSRF protection via the existing form's hidden `csrf_token`).
- **`scan-camera-toggle` styled with the existing `class="button"` from `base.html`.** No new CSS. The button visually matches the existing "Find item" submit button + the action-link buttons on the resolved-item picker — visual consistency is free.

---

**Self-critique notes (rolling) — SC1d:**

- **Whitelist is two-pattern + simple, not a URL parser.** `_safe_scan_next(raw)` returns `raw` if `raw == "/scan"` or `raw.startswith("/scan/")`, else `None`. Pinned by the four whitelist tests per route (12 total): `/scan/item/{id}` ✓, `/scan` ✓, `/admin/items/X/edit` → fallback, `//evil.com/x` → fallback. Using `urllib.parse.urlsplit` would parse `//evil.com/x` as `(scheme='', netloc='evil.com', path='/x')` and need a netloc check; the two-prefix string check is simpler and the integration tests directly pin the threat case. Revisit if a future scan-flow URL doesn't fit either pattern (none currently planned).
- **Whitelist allows `/scan/<arbitrary-id>` even if the id doesn't exist.** A user crafting `next=/scan/item/999999` would land on a 404 from `GET /scan/item/{id}`. Not a security issue (404 is the expected behaviour for missing items, same as if they typed the URL directly). UX cost: a malicious or confused caller could redirect a successful submit to a 404 page. Acceptable v1 — the only legitimate caller is `scan.html` which sets the value to the same item the user just acted on.
- **`next` is dropped on the error path** (insufficient stock on `out` and `adjust direction=decrease`). Pinned by `test_insufficient_stock_drops_next_and_re_renders` + `test_insufficient_stock_decrease_drops_next_and_re_renders`. Trade-off: the user lands on the per-action form with the canonical error context (open value, recent movements, in-form error block) instead of staying in scan flow. Threading `next` to the re-render would need helper + template + test changes for a rare path. Acceptable v1 cost; flagged. If a future complaint surfaces ("I scanned out too many and got bumped out of scan flow"), threading `next` through `_render_stock_*_form` is ~10-15 LoC + one template change + 2 tests across the two error paths.
- **`next` is also silently dropped on validation 400s** (empty qty, malformed unit_cost, etc.) — those raise `HTTPException(400)` directly via the parse helpers, before the redirect is constructed. Same posture as today's behaviour for any other form that has hidden fields; consistent with the "validation 400 means the user fixes their input and resubmits" mental model.
- **No per-action form template changes.** The `next` form param defaults to `""` and is only set by `scan.html`. The per-action form templates (`stock_in_form.html` / `stock_out_form.html` / `stock_adjust_form.html`) don't render a hidden `next` input — they would always be empty there. Trade-off: a user navigating from the per-action form to scan and back never carries scan context; the only way to land back in scan flow after a movement is to start the movement from scan. Documented; not a regression (today's behaviour is the same).
- **Three near-identical 1-line changes across the three POST routes.** Could centralise via a helper like `_redirect_back(item, action, next_) -> RedirectResponse`. At three call sites the duplication is ~3 LoC × 3 = 9 LoC vs a 5-LoC helper used three times. The inline form is more readable (the redirect target is right there next to the flash); the helper would force a reader to context-switch. Not extracting; the boundary feels right for v1. Same posture as the `_flash` helper (currently duplicated across multiple routers — flagged in S1's self-critique but acceptable until the cost of duplication exceeds the cost of an indirection).
- **`alias="next"` keeps the URL form name as `next` while the Python identifier is `next_`** (avoid the builtin shadow). FastAPI's `Form(default, alias=...)` is the standard mechanism for this; mypy strict didn't flag it. The underscore-suffix convention is already used elsewhere in the codebase for the same reason (`from_, type_, etc.). Documented in self-critique only — the name change isn't an API surface, just a Python identifier choice.
- **Engine isolation preserved.** None of the existing happy-path tests for stock-in / stock-out / stock-adjust pass a `next` value; they continue to assert the old default redirect target (`/admin/items/{id}/<action>`). The new `TestStock*NextRedirect` classes are additive — no existing test reshape needed. Pinned by `1677 passed (was 1661, +16 new, 0 reshaped)`.
- **No e2e walk added.** The redirect-target chain is integration-test territory; an e2e walk that drove a scan-flow form submission and asserted the post-submit page would re-test what `test_scan_routes.py` (action-picker render) + `test_movements_routes.py::TestStock*NextRedirect` (redirect target) already pin in isolation. The e2e walk for the round-trip scan-flow chain (scan → submit → land back on `/scan/item/{id}` → see post-mutation qty → scan next code) lands when SC2 introduces camera-side behaviour worth covering — at that point there's a unique full-flow story to tell.
- **`scan.html` carries `value="/scan/item/{id}"` literal in three forms; could centralise via a Jinja `{% set %}`.** Three identical hidden inputs differing only by being inside three separate forms. Hoisting to a `{% set scan_next_url = ... %}` at the top would save 0 LoC (the value is reused but the input element still has to be rendered three times) and add a name to look up. Not centralising. Same posture as the three identical CSRF hidden inputs already in the template.
- **Maintainability**: ~30 LoC of clean addition to `app/movements.py` (~5 helper + ~3 per route × 3 = ~15) + 3 LoC to `scan.html`. A competent dev can read the slice in under 5 minutes and understand the redirect-target threading. The four design decisions (Q1-Q4) are documented inline in PROGRESS.md as part of the slice plan; the helper docstring summarises Q2's whitelist policy. **Boring is good.**
- **No CSRF concern beyond the existing middleware.** The hidden `next` input is a regular form field that the standard double-submit cookie protects uniformly with the rest of the form. Pinned indirectly by the existing happy-path tests on the three routes (which all use `_csrf(client)` to seed the cookie + form token).
- **Open redirect threat is the main security concern; pinned by 3 tests.** `test_next_open_redirect_attempt_falls_back` on each route asserts that `next=//evil.com/x` falls back to the per-action form redirect. The whitelist's "must start with `/scan/` or equal `/scan`" wording covers `//evil.com/x` (doesn't start with `/`-then-`scan`), `https://evil.com` (also not), and `/scanner/...` (close but not `/scan/`). Documented in `_safe_scan_next`'s docstring.

---

<!-- SC1c plan (now shipped) — kept commented for audit-trail context only.

**SC1c — Inline action forms on the scan-flow item page (DoD #3 desktop/USB leg, MISSION §3 "Barcode/QR workflow"):** continues SC1b's `/scan/item/{id}` action-picker page. Replaces the three action *links* (Stock-out / Stock-in / Adjust) with three inline *forms* that POST directly to the existing `/admin/items/{id}/{out,in,adjust}` movement routes. After SC1c the flow on a USB-scanner desktop is **scan-Enter → fill qty (and unit_cost where required) → submit** — two interactions. The check-out link stays as a link for flagged items (separate flow with its own state machine). SC2 adds the camera leg of DoD #3 on mobile.

**Why 3a (three inline forms) over 3b (one form with action selector) or 3c (default action with alternates):**
- 3a satisfies DoD #3's "two interactions" goal directly: the user types into the qty box of the action they want; there's no separate "pick action" click.
- 3b would need either a re-render round-trip or JS to swap the cost field based on action — MISSION §5 forbids JS frameworks; HTMX is allowed but the conditional shape adds a concept the next dev would have to learn for marginal gain.
- 3c forces a wrong default 1/3 of the time (Workshop's hot-path is stock-out, but Office uses scan for stock-in too) and re-introduces the link-click for the non-default cases.
- Trade-off: 3a is visually busier with three stacked forms. Acceptable on the scan-flow surface (a destination page, not a list) and on the 10" tablet target (each form is short — out has 1 input, in has 2, adjust has 4). Each form is independent; pressing Enter inside a form input submits its parent form, not its neighbour.

**Action ordering** (top to bottom): Stock-out first (Workshop's hot-path: consuming raw material in production), Stock-in second, Adjust third (variance corrections — least common, also the largest form so it sits at the bottom). Note this is the inverse of `items_form.html`'s action block (which orders in / out / adjust); the reordering reflects scan-flow's hot-path bias.

**Forms surface only the required inputs per action.** Optional fields (note, reason for in/out) are dropped from the inline forms — users who need to attach a note can navigate via the existing per-action form (still reachable at `/admin/items/{id}/in` etc, and the form actions on the inline forms point there so a successful submit lands the user on that page where they can add follow-up movements). Adjust's `reason` *is* inline because it's required server-side and is the variance attribution; a scan-flow Adjust still needs that field. `unit_cost` is required for `direction=increase` and ignored for `direction=decrease` server-side; the inline form renders the input always, same as the existing `stock_adjust_form.html`.

- **Template** (`app/templates/scan.html` — extended):
  - Replace the three `<a class="button" data-testid="scan-action-{in,out,adjust}">` link blocks with three `<form method="post" action="/admin/items/{id}/{out,in,adjust}">` blocks, ordered out → in → adjust.
  - Each form carries the standard `<input type="hidden" name="csrf_token" value="{{ csrf_token }}">`.
  - **Stock-out form**: `<section data-testid="scan-out-form">` with one `<input data-testid="scan-out-qty-input" name="qty" type="text" inputmode="decimal" required placeholder="qty">` + a `<button data-testid="scan-out-submit">Stock out</button>`. The `inputmode="decimal"` lifts the numeric keypad on mobile keyboards.
  - **Stock-in form**: `<section data-testid="scan-in-form">` with `<input data-testid="scan-in-qty-input" name="qty">` + `<input data-testid="scan-in-unit-cost-input" name="unit_cost">` + `<button data-testid="scan-in-submit">Stock in</button>`. Both inputs `required` + `inputmode="decimal"`.
  - **Adjust form**: `<section data-testid="scan-adjust-form">` with `<select data-testid="scan-adjust-direction-input" name="direction" required>` (blank `— pick one —` then `increase` / `decrease`) + `<input data-testid="scan-adjust-qty-input" name="qty">` + `<input data-testid="scan-adjust-unit-cost-input" name="unit_cost">` (not `required` because decrease ignores it) + `<input data-testid="scan-adjust-reason-input" name="reason" required maxlength="255">` + `<button data-testid="scan-adjust-submit">Adjust</button>`.
  - **No route changes** — `app/movements.py`'s `record_stock_in` / `record_stock_out` / `record_stock_adjustment` already handle validation, audit, redirect. The inline forms post to those routes unchanged. On success, the existing routes redirect to their per-action form (`/admin/items/{id}/in` etc) with a flash; the user lands there, sees the recent-movements table for confirmation, and can navigate back to scan via the nav. **Out of scope: a `next=` redirect param to keep the user in scan flow** — flagged as a future polish slice (SC1d?), since threading it would touch four routes' tests and isn't required to satisfy DoD #3's "two interactions".
  - **Archived items**: same posture as SC1b — no action forms rendered (the underlying routes 400 on archived items, so submitting would error). The archived badge + explanatory note + scan input persist so the user can scan another item.
  - The `scan-action-checkout` link stays as-is for `requires_checkout` items.
  - The scan input + autofocus stay at the top of the page so the next item's scan keystroke is captured without manual nav.

- **Tests updated** (`tests/integration/test_scan_routes.py`):
  - `TestScanItemPageRender::test_renders_three_action_links_with_correct_hrefs` renamed to `test_renders_three_inline_action_forms` and rewritten to assert each form's `action` attribute + each submit button's test-id (instead of asserting link hrefs + scan-action-{in,out,adjust} test-ids).
  - `TestScanItemPageArchived::test_archived_item_omits_action_buttons` updated: now asserts `scan-out-submit`, `scan-in-submit`, `scan-adjust-submit` are absent (was: `scan-action-in/-out/-adjust`). `scan-action-checkout` assertion stays since checkout remains a link.
  - `TestScanItemPageResolveChain::test_post_resolve_then_follow_renders_action_picker` updated: asserts `scan-out-form` is present (was: `scan-action-in`).

- **Tests added** (~13 new in `tests/integration/test_scan_routes.py`):
  - `TestScanItemPageInlineForms` (3): each of out / in / adjust renders with `method="post"` + `action="/admin/items/{id}/..."` + a CSRF hidden input.
  - `TestScanItemPageInlineFormFields` (~6): out form has qty input only (no unit_cost / no reason / no direction); in form has qty + unit_cost (no direction / no reason); adjust form has direction select + qty + unit_cost + reason; adjust direction select offers `increase` + `decrease` options; the qty inputs on out/in are `required`; the reason input on adjust is `required`.
  - `TestScanItemPageInlineFormSubmission` (~4): Workshop submits the inline stock-out form (POSTs to `/admin/items/{id}/out` with qty=2 → 303 to `/admin/items/{id}/out` + audit row written + current_qty bumped down by the engine); same for stock-in (with unit_cost → audit row written + current_qty bumped up + cost layer created); same for adjust direction=increase (audit + layer); insufficient stock on adjust=decrease re-renders the per-action form's error path (existing route behaviour, but pinned for the chain).

- **Repo health target**: ruff clean; mypy clean (28 source files unchanged); pytest unit + integration ~1660 passing (was 1648, net +~12 after 3 existing-test updates and ~13 new); Playwright 14 passing (no e2e walk this slice — the inline-form chain is integration territory; an e2e walk lands once the next= polish keeps users in scan flow on success).

- **DoD impact**: SC1c closes the desktop/USB leg of DoD #3. Workshop scanning on a desktop with a USB scanner can now record an in/out/adjust movement in two interactions (scan-Enter, then submit-the-action-form). The remaining gap is SC2 — camera-based scanning on mobile. Once SC2 lands, DoD #3 ticks.

---

**Self-critique notes (rolling) — SC1c:**

- **DoD #3 desktop/USB leg closed; mobile leg still open.** SC1c delivers the two-interaction goal for the USB-scanner case: scan-Enter (interaction 1), fill qty + submit (interaction 2). The mobile/camera leg (SC2) and the post-submit "stay in scan flow" polish (SC1d, see below) are still ahead. **Conservatively not ticking DoD #3** — it requires "USB scanner on desktop AND camera on a phone" (MISSION §7), and the camera leg has zero coverage today.
- **Post-submit redirect lands on the per-action form, not back in scan flow.** A successful inline submit of stock-out from `/scan/item/123` redirects to `/admin/items/123/out` (the existing route's redirect target). The user lands there with a flash + recent-movements table; to scan the next item they have to click the Scan nav link. **Two interactions per movement is satisfied** — DoD #3's wording is "record an in, out, or adjustment movement in two interactions", not "scan an unbounded sequence of items in two interactions each". A multi-item scan session pays one extra nav-click per item to return to scan flow. Flagged for SC1d polish — thread an optional `next=` redirect param through the in/out/adjust routes so scan-flow submits land back on `/scan/item/{id}` (or `/scan` itself, for the next-item case). Touches four routes' tests; queued in Next slice.
- **Insufficient-stock error path doesn't re-render on the scan-flow surface.** Submitting stock-out for more than `current_qty` triggers the existing route's `InsufficientStockError` rollback path, which re-renders `stock_out_form.html` (the FULL per-action form) with a 400 + error block. The user lands away from scan flow but with the canonical error context. Same posture as the post-submit redirect — DoD #3's two-interaction goal is unaffected; the recoverable error pulls the user out of scan flow into the bigger form. Acceptable v1; flagged.
- **Three forms over one with action selector (3a vs 3b) was the right call.** 3b would have meant either a JS swap (banned by MISSION §5) or a re-render round-trip (extra GET on every action-pick). 3a's "visually busier" cost is small in practice — each form is ≤4 inputs, and the 10" tablet target shows all three above the fold. The DoD wording explicitly says "two interactions"; 3a satisfies it directly without a "pick action" interaction.
- **Action ordering (out → in → adjust) inverts `items_form.html`'s in → out → adjust block.** Deliberate: scan-flow's hot-path is workshop *consuming* materials (stock-out), not workshop *receiving* materials (stock-in is mostly Office). Putting stock-out at the top of the scan-flow page means a Workshop user's eye lands on the right form first. Documented inline in the template; pinned indirectly by the test that asserts the relative position of out/in/adjust markers in the rendered HTML (`test_stock_out_form_has_qty_input_only` + `test_stock_in_form_has_qty_and_unit_cost` use marker comparisons).
- **Optional fields (note, optional reason for in/out) dropped from the inline forms.** Workshop's hot-path doesn't usually need these. Users who do can navigate to the full per-action form (still reachable at `/admin/items/{id}/in` etc); the inline-form action URLs land them on that page after submit, where they can record a follow-up movement with a note. The trade-off is documented in the slice plan; if a recurring "I forgot the note" complaint surfaces, the field is one line of template to add.
- **Adjust unit_cost rendered always but only required for `direction=increase`** — same posture as the existing `stock_adjust_form.html`. The route ignores it for decrease (consumption price is per-layer FIFO). A user filling unit_cost for a decrease has their input silently dropped; the helper `<em>` block explains "required for increases; ignored for decreases" inline. Could split into two adjust forms (one per direction) but that doubles the form count for marginal UX gain and breaks the "this is the same shape as the per-action form" intuition.
- **No e2e walk added.** Same posture as SC1a + SC1b — integration tests exhaustively cover the form rendering shape, the field set, the required attributes, and the four submit-chain scenarios (stock-in / stock-out / adjust-increase / 400 path). An e2e walk that drove a click on `scan-out-submit` would re-test what `test_movements_e2e.py` already pins for the stock-out route. The e2e walk lands once SC1d's `next=` polish keeps users on scan-flow after a successful submit; at that point the chain (scan → submit → land back on /scan/item/X with flash → scan next item) is unique to scan flow and worth walking.
- **Maintainability**: the slice is template-only — zero new modules, zero new routes, zero new helpers. `scan.html` grew by ~110 lines (three form blocks replacing three link blocks); the test extension is ~280 lines (16 new tests + 3 reshaped). A competent dev can read the slice in under 10 minutes and understand the inline-form-to-existing-route chain. **Boring is good.**
- **No CSRF concern beyond the existing middleware.** Each form renders `csrf_token` from the standard context processor; the middleware double-submit cookie protection covers all three POSTs uniformly. Pinned indirectly by the role-enforcement tests on the existing in/out/adjust routes — they were already passing for the Workshop POST chain.
- **`required` attribute on qty + reason inputs is browser-side only.** Server-side validation in `app/movements.py` is the authoritative gate (blank → 400 with a clear message). Browser-side `required` saves a round-trip on the obvious-empty case. A user with JS disabled / a custom client still hits the route's 400. Pinned by `test_required_attributes_on_qty_inputs` + `test_adjust_reason_input_is_required` (template-level) and `test_inline_form_reaches_route_validation_path` (route-level 400).
- **`maxlength="255"` on the adjust reason input** matches the existing `stock_adjust_form.html` value and the underlying column cap. The reason column is `String(255)` per the schema; no chance of a server-truncate surprise.
- **Three submit buttons on one page is fine — submitting one form does not submit the others.** Each form is its own `<form>` element with its own action URL. Pressing Enter inside an input only submits its parent form. Browsers don't broadcast submits across forms. This is HTML-101 but worth flagging because the visual presentation of three forms close together on one page can superficially suggest otherwise.

<!-- SC1b plan (now shipped) — kept commented for audit-trail context only.

**SC1b — Scan resolve to action picker on the scan-landing page (DoD #3 second step, MISSION §3 "Barcode/QR workflow"):** continues SC1a toward DoD #3's two-interaction goal. Replaces SC1a's `POST /scan/resolve → 303 to /admin/items/{id}/edit` chain with `POST /scan/resolve → 303 to /scan/item/{id}` plus a new `GET /scan/item/{id}` action-picker page. After SC1b the flow is **scan → action button → action form**: still three interactions but the resolve+pick step lives on a single scan-flow surface. SC1c will fold qty/cost entry inline so the entire flow collapses to two interactions.

**Why a new URL `/scan/item/{id}` instead of rendering directly on POST**: keeps the POST-redirect-GET pattern. Refreshing the action-picker page after a successful scan must not re-POST `/scan/resolve` (which would re-resolve and re-redirect, harmless but ugly browser warning). A GET URL also makes the surface bookmarkable / shareable for triage workflows ("hey here's the scan page for item 42"). The existing 303 status on `POST /scan/resolve` is preserved; only the redirect *target* changes.

- **Route module** (`app/scan.py`):
  - **`POST /scan/resolve`** — same role gate, same trim, same flash semantics for empty/no-match. **Changed**: on a successful resolve, redirect target flips from `/admin/items/{item.id}/edit` to `/scan/item/{item.id}`. The `_resolve_code` helper is unchanged (qr_code-first then sku-fallback, archived items still resolve).
  - **`GET /scan/item/{item_id}`** (new) — `Depends(require_role(Role.WORKSHOP, Role.OFFICE, Role.MANAGER))` (Admin via the role bypass; pending → 403; anon → 401). Loads `Item` by id; 404 if missing. Renders `scan.html` with `resolved_item=item` in the context. Read-only — no audit. The route is a *thin GET* — no query params, no form processing; its only job is to present the action picker for an already-resolved item.
  - Both routes share the existing `_resolve_code` helper unchanged.
  - **No new helper for the item lookup**: `db.get(Item, item_id)` is the SQLAlchemy 2.x point-lookup; raising 404 inline is ~3 lines and used by every other `/admin/items/{id}/...` route in the codebase.

- **Template** (`app/templates/scan.html` — extended):
  - Existing form block (`<form method="post" action="/scan/resolve">`) stays at the top with `autofocus` preserved so a USB scanner on the action-picker page can still drive a scan-of-the-next-item without manual nav. The user's flow is: scan item A → land on `/scan/item/A` → click action → done. If they want item B next, they scan from any scan-flow page; the input is always focused.
  - **New conditional block** below the form: `{% if resolved_item %} ... {% endif %}` rendering an item identity + action picker.
    - Item identity card: `<div data-testid="scan-resolved-item" data-item-id="{{ resolved_item.id }}">` containing `<strong>{{ resolved_item.sku }}</strong>` + `{{ resolved_item.name }}` + current qty/unit. If `resolved_item.archived_at` is set, also render `<span data-testid="scan-resolved-archived-badge">archived</span>`.
    - Action buttons (links styled as buttons): each rendered only when the item is **not archived** because the underlying `/in`, `/out`, `/adjust` routes all `_reject_archived` with HTTP 400. Linking to an action that would 400 is a dead-end; better to surface the archived state and offer no action button.
      - `<a href="/admin/items/{{ resolved_item.id }}/in" data-testid="scan-action-in">Stock in →</a>`
      - `<a href="/admin/items/{{ resolved_item.id }}/out" data-testid="scan-action-out">Stock out →</a>`
      - `<a href="/admin/items/{{ resolved_item.id }}/adjust" data-testid="scan-action-adjust">Adjust →</a>`
      - Optional `<a href="/admin/items/{{ resolved_item.id }}/checkout" data-testid="scan-action-checkout">Check out →</a>` rendered iff `resolved_item.requires_checkout`. The check-out form (C2) has its own gating; surfacing it here is a polish detail that keeps the flow consistent with `items_form.html`'s action block.
    - For an archived item: the identity card renders + the archived badge, **no action buttons**, plus a one-line note `<em data-testid="scan-resolved-archived-note">This item is archived; record movements via the items list instead.</em>` so the user understands why the actions are missing.
  - The flash region from `base.html` continues to handle "no match" / "empty code" feedback after a 303 to `/scan`. The action-picker page itself doesn't flash on render (it's a destination, not a transition).

- **Router wiring** (`app/main.py`): no change — `app.include_router(scan_module.router)` already covers the new route under the `/scan` prefix.

- **Test coverage** (target ~17 new in `tests/integration/test_scan_routes.py`; ~8 existing redirect-target assertions updated):
  - **Updated existing tests** (8 assertions changed from `/admin/items/{id}/edit` to `/scan/item/{id}`): `TestScanResolveRoleEnforcement` (workshop/office/manager — 3); `TestScanResolveMatching` (by_qr/by_sku/qr_wins/trim/archived — 5).
  - `TestScanItemPageRoleEnforcement` (5): anon 401, pending 403, Workshop/Office/Manager 200.
  - `TestScanItemPageRender` (4): renders `scan-resolved-item` block; renders `scan-action-in` / `-out` / `-adjust` links with the correct hrefs; the heading + scan input are still rendered (so the user can scan-another).
  - `TestScanItemPageRequiresCheckout` (2): flagged item shows `scan-action-checkout`; non-flagged item omits it.
  - `TestScanItemPageArchived` (3): archived item shows `scan-resolved-archived-badge` and `scan-resolved-archived-note`; archived item omits all action buttons; archived item still renders the scan input (so the user can scan another item).
  - `TestScanItemPageNotFound` (1): GET `/scan/item/999999` → 404.
  - `TestScanItemPageReadOnly` (1): GET writes no audit row.
  - `TestScanItemPageResolveChainCsrf` (1): the `POST /scan/resolve → /scan/item/{id}` chain end-to-end (post, follow redirect, verify the action picker renders the resolved item).

- **Repo health target**: ruff clean; mypy clean (28 source files unchanged — extending the existing `app/scan.py`, no new module); pytest unit + integration ~1649 passing (was 1632, +~17); Playwright 14 passing (the resolve→pick chain is integration-test territory; an e2e walk lands when SC1c collapses qty/cost entry inline so the chain has unique behaviour to walk that integration can't pin alone).

- **DoD impact**: SC1b advances DoD #3 from "Workshop has a focused-input scan landing page that resolves a code to the existing edit surface" (SC1a) to "Workshop scans → lands on a scan-flow action picker → clicks the action they want". The remaining gap to DoD #3's two-interaction goal is SC1c (qty + unit cost entry inline on the scan-flow surface) + SC2 (camera-based scanning on mobile).

-->

---

**Self-critique notes (rolling) — SC1b:**

- **DoD #3 still demands "two interactions"; SC1b delivers three.** Scan + Enter is one; clicking the action button is two; submitting the qty form is three. SC1b is the second of three sub-slices that progressively collapse the chain. It moves the resolve+pick step onto a single in-flow surface (SC1a still sent the user to `/admin/items/{id}/edit`, which mixed scan-flow with the items CRUD edit form). SC1c will fold qty + unit-cost entry inline so the action button submits the movement directly. Documented; flagged.
- **`/scan/item/{id}` chosen over rendering directly on POST** to preserve POST-redirect-GET. A direct render would mean refreshing the action-picker re-POSTs `/scan/resolve` (idempotent — same item resolves to the same redirect — but throws a browser warning + an unnecessary DB query). The new GET URL is also bookmarkable / shareable for triage workflows ("here's the scan page for item 42"). The trade-off is one extra route + one extra round-trip; acceptable v1 cost for the UX win.
- **Action buttons omitted on archived items**, deliberately. The `/in`, `/out`, `/adjust` routes all `_reject_archived` with HTTP 400 (movements.py:212-215). Linking from the picker would be a dead-end. The archived state instead surfaces a banner (`scan-resolved-archived-badge`) + an explanatory note (`scan-resolved-archived-note`) telling the user to use the items list. Could later add an "Unarchive" link if Manager — deferred (action-picker is read-flow; unarchive is admin-flow on the items page).
- **Archived item still 303-resolves to `/scan/item/{id}`** rather than redirecting to `/scan` with a flash. Rationale: a scanner doesn't know an item was archived, and the action-picker page surfaces the archived state explicitly (badge + note + omitted buttons). A flash-on-/scan would force the user to re-scan (or worse, scan a different item to break the cycle). Pinned by `TestScanResolveMatching::test_archived_item_still_resolves` + `TestScanItemPageArchived`'s 3 tests.
- **`scan-action-checkout` rendered conditionally on `requires_checkout`.** The check-out form (C2) has its own role + state gate; the picker just exposes the link when the flag is set, mirroring `items_form.html`'s action block. Pinned by `TestScanItemPageRequiresCheckout`'s 2 tests (flagged shows; non-flagged omits). Note: the link is rendered for *every* role that can see the picker (Workshop / Office / Manager / Admin), since C2's role gate is at the route level not the link level — same posture as `items_form.html`.
- **Scan input + autofocus retained on `/scan/item/{id}`** so a USB scanner can drive a fresh resolve from the picker page without manual nav back to `/scan`. Pinned by `TestScanItemPageRender::test_scan_input_still_rendered_so_next_scan_works` + `TestScanItemPageArchived::test_archived_item_still_renders_scan_input`. Trade-off: two `<input autofocus>` elements on the page would be wrong, but the picker page only has one (the form's input); the action-picker section uses `<a>` links, not focusable inputs. Acceptable.
- **No e2e walk added.** Same posture as SC1a: integration tests pin the role matrix, render shape, archived behaviour, requires_checkout fork, 404, read-only invariant, and the full POST→follow chain. An e2e walk that drove a click on a `scan-action-in` link would re-test what existing `test_movements_e2e.py` already pins for the action-form side. The e2e walk lands when SC1c creates a unique flow (qty entry on the scan surface) — at that point there's a chain to walk that no single existing e2e exercises.
- **`db.get(Item, item_id)` used directly, no helper.** Three lines: `item = db.get(Item, item_id); if item is None: raise HTTPException(404, ...)`. Inline is fine at one call site; if a future scan-flow route needs the same lookup, extract to `_get_item_or_404` (already exists in `app/movements.py` for the `/admin/items/{id}/...` routes — could reach across modules but the boundaries are clean as-is).
- **PT018 (compound assert) bit again in the new tests.** `test_renders_three_action_links_with_correct_hrefs` originally chained `assert (href in text and testid in text)`; the lint check caught it on the first run and I split into six separate asserts (one per substring). Same root cause as iteration 47's chore — the loop runner's `make check` is the gating signal. **Take-away for future slices**: write each conjunct as its own assert from the start to avoid the back-and-forth.
- **Three `assert ... in resp.text` per action link** (six asserts for in/out/adjust) is verbose but each surfaces a distinct failure mode: missing href tells you the URL changed; missing test-id tells you the template structure changed. A tighter "build the expected attribute substring once" helper would save lines but obscure failure messages. Acceptable verbosity.
- **`HTMLResponse` import added** to the existing `from fastapi.responses import HTMLResponse, RedirectResponse, Response` line — no actual change, since the new `scan_item_page` returns `HTMLResponse` (already imported). The decorator `response_class=HTMLResponse` is also pre-existing. Net: one new `HTTPException` import on the `from fastapi import` line.
- **Maintainability**: the new route is 13 LoC including the docstring; the template extension is ~50 LoC; the test extension is ~150 LoC. A competent dev could read the slice in under five minutes and understand exactly what changed. The `/scan/item/{id}` URL is self-documenting. Boring is good.



<!-- SC1a plan (now shipped) — kept commented for audit-trail context only.

**SC1a — Scan-mode landing page with code-resolution (DoD #3 first step):** smallest end-to-end SC1 sub-slice. New module `app/scan.py` mounted at `/scan` with two routes (`GET /scan` renders the page; `POST /scan/resolve` resolves a code to an item and 303-redirects to its existing edit page). New template `scan.html`. New nav link `nav-scan`.

Why this sub-slice and not full SC1: DoD #3 calls out "in two interactions". The actual two-interaction flow (scan → action button which submits the movement) requires merging the action picker + qty entry + unit-cost prompt onto the scan-landing surface, which is genuinely too big for a single iteration and forks on the USB-vs-camera UX question (the Backlog explicitly notes SC1 "deserves dedicated brainstorming"). SC1a takes the smallest *first* step that's verifiable on its own: establish the scan-mode URL, give USB scanners a focused input that submits on Enter, and connect a resolved code to the existing per-item action surface. Workshop already has read-only access to `/admin/items/{id}/edit` (per I1c) which already exposes the in/out/adjust action links — so SC1a delivers a complete *three-interaction* end-to-end path (scan → click action → submit form) that moves DoD #3 from completely unmoved to substantially closer. Subsequent slices (SC1b: action picker on scan page; SC1c: qty entry + unit-cost prompt; SC2: camera scanning) progressively collapse the path to two interactions.

- **Route module** (`app/scan.py`):
  - `router = APIRouter(prefix="/scan", tags=["scan"])`.
  - `GET /scan` — `Depends(require_role(Role.WORKSHOP, Role.OFFICE, Role.MANAGER))` (Admin via the role bypass; pending → 403; anon → 401). Renders `scan.html`. Read-only — no audit.
  - `POST /scan/resolve` — same role gate. Form param `code: str = Form("")`. Trims leading/trailing whitespace. If empty after trim → `_flash("Please scan or type a code.")` + 303 to `/scan`. Else looks up `Item` by `qr_code == code` (single-row exact match — the model has a partial-unique index on `qr_code WHERE qr_code IS NOT NULL`), falling back to `Item.sku == code` (the model has a unique index). On match: 303 to `/admin/items/{item.id}/edit`. On no match: `_flash("No item found for code: {code}.")` + 303 to `/scan`.
  - **Precedence is qr_code-first then sku-fallback.** Rationale: physical labels carry a QR code; the QR's payload is the canonical scanned value. SKUs are human-typed identifiers (e.g. "ALLOY-925-2MM") and would be entered manually only as a fallback when no QR is present. If both indexes happened to match different items (extremely unlikely given the unique constraints across distinct columns, but conceivable if a manager set sku="X" on item A and qr_code="X" on item B), the qr_code match wins. Pinned by `TestScanResolvePrecedence`.
  - **Archived items still resolve.** A scanner doesn't know an item was archived; refusing the resolution would leave the user staring at the scan page with no signal as to why. The destination edit page (`/admin/items/{id}/edit`) already renders archived items in a read-only state with a clear `archived` badge, so the user lands on a useful surface. Pinned by `TestScanResolveArchivedItem`. (A future polish slice could flash a warning on resolution; deferred — the destination page is already explicit.)
  - Read-only: neither route writes an audit row. Resolution is a navigation action, not a state change. Pinned by `TestScanReadOnly`.

- **Template** (`app/templates/scan.html`):
  - Extends `base.html`.
  - `<h1 data-testid="scan-heading">Scan</h1>`.
  - `<p data-testid="scan-instructions">` with one line of guidance ("Scan an item's QR code or type its SKU and press Enter.").
  - `<form data-testid="scan-form" method="post" action="/scan/resolve">` with the standard CSRF token hidden input (matches the existing pattern from `locations_form.html` etc.) and one input `<input data-testid="scan-code-input" name="code" type="text" autocomplete="off" autofocus required>`. Submit button `data-testid="scan-submit"`.
  - `autofocus` is the USB-scanner-friendly choice: HID-emulating scanners send keystrokes followed by Enter/Tab; landing on the page with the input focused means the very next keystroke is captured. Camera-based scanning (SC2) will overlay a different control on the same page.
  - The flash region from `base.html` is reused for the "no match" / "empty code" feedback — no per-template error block needed.

- **Nav link** (`base.html`):
  - `<a href="/scan" data-testid="nav-scan">` inserted as the *second* item (right after "Home"), visible to **Workshop, Office, Manager, Admin** (i.e. every active non-pending role). Workshop today only sees "Home" + "Items" — putting Scan second pushes it onto Workshop's hot-path. For other roles it's still a useful primary surface. Active-state highlighting via `aria-current="page"` when `request.url.path == "/scan"`.

- **Router wiring**: `app.include_router(scan_module.router)` added to `app/main.py` next to the other includes.

- **Test coverage** (target ~22 new in `tests/integration/test_scan_routes.py`):
  - `TestScanGetRoleEnforcement` (6): anon 401, pending 403, Workshop 200, Office 200, Manager 200, Admin 200.
  - `TestScanGetRender` (3): heading present, form action `/scan/resolve` and method `post`, input has `autofocus` + `name="code"`.
  - `TestScanResolveRoleEnforcement` (5): anon 401, pending 403, Workshop 303, Office 303, Manager 303 (with a valid code in each case for the allowed roles).
  - `TestScanResolveByQrCode` (1): seed item with `qr_code="QR123"`, POST with `code=QR123`, assert 303 to `/admin/items/{id}/edit`.
  - `TestScanResolveBySku` (1): seed item with `sku="SKU-A"` and no qr_code, POST with `code=SKU-A`, assert 303 to `/admin/items/{id}/edit`.
  - `TestScanResolvePrecedence` (1): two items — A with `sku="X"`, B with `qr_code="X"`. POST with `code=X` resolves to B (qr_code wins).
  - `TestScanResolveTrimsWhitespace` (1): POST with `code="  QR123  "` resolves to the QR123 item.
  - `TestScanResolveEmptyCode` (1): POST with empty code → 303 to `/scan` + flash.
  - `TestScanResolveNoMatch` (1): POST with garbage code → 303 to `/scan` + flash that includes the offending code.
  - `TestScanResolveArchivedItem` (1): POST resolves an archived item → still 303 to `/admin/items/{id}/edit`.
  - `TestScanReadOnly` (2): GET writes no audit row; POST resolve writes no audit row (compares pre/post counts).
  - `TestScanNav` (4): nav-scan visible to Workshop, Office, Manager, Admin (one each); absent for pending; absent for anon (no nav at all). Confirms current-page highlighting on `/scan`.

- **Repo health target**: ruff clean; mypy clean (28 source files, +1 module: `app/scan.py`); pytest unit + integration ~1623 passing (was 1601, +~22); Playwright 14 passing (no e2e walk added — the scan flow's two-touch nature is integration-test territory; an e2e walk for the full scan-resolve-act flow lands in SC1b once there's a unique end-to-end story to tell).

-->

---

**Self-critique notes (rolling) — SC1a:**

- **DoD #3 wording is "two interactions"; SC1a delivers three.** Scan-input-and-Enter is one; clicking the action link on the redirect target is two; submitting the in/out/adjust form is three. SC1a is a foundation slice — it gets the URL, the focused input, and the resolve→item-detail wiring in place. SC1b will fold the action picker onto the scan-landing page so resolution + action-selection collapse into one interaction; SC1c will add qty/unit-cost entry inline so the entire flow is two interactions (scan + submit-the-action). The split is genuinely useful: each sub-slice has independent test coverage and can be reverted alone, where bundling all three would make a 600-LoC PR with intertwined concerns. Documented; flagged for SC1b.
- **No e2e walk this slice.** Decision: integration tests already cover all the meaningful paths (resolve-by-qr, resolve-by-sku, precedence, trim, archived, empty, no-match, role matrix, nav visibility). An e2e walk that drives the full scan→action-link→form-submit chain would re-test what `test_items_e2e.py` already pins for the action-form side and what `test_scan_routes.py` pins for the resolve side. The e2e walk lands when SC1b creates a unique scan-side flow (action picker on the same surface) — at that point there's a chain to walk that no single existing e2e exercises. Flagged in PROGRESS.
- **`name="code"` shadows the Python builtin `code` in the route signature.** Same wart as the `format` shadow in 8 prior CSV-export sites. Renaming the form field would break the URL convention (it's the natural form name). The shadow is harmless because the route never calls the builtin. Acceptable.
- **No CSRF concern on the resolve POST.** The standard double-submit cookie middleware (`CSRFMiddleware` in `app/main.py`) protects all POSTs uniformly; the scan template renders `csrf_token` from the context processor. Pinned indirectly by the role-enforcement tests (anon POST with a CSRF cookie still 401s on auth, before any audit could be written).
- **Empty / no-match flow flashes back to `/scan` rather than re-rendering inline.** Trade-off: a flash + redirect costs an extra round-trip vs. a 200 with the error message inline, but it preserves the GET-on-render invariant (refreshing the page after a failed lookup doesn't re-POST), keeps the autofocus reset cleanly, and uses the same `data-testid="flash"` surface that every other route uses. The integration tests pin both the 303 + the post-redirect flash visibility. Acceptable.
- **`autofocus` is set on the input but not re-asserted after a failed scan redirect.** When the user lands on `/scan` after a flash redirect, the same template renders with `autofocus`, so the next keystroke from the scanner is captured. Manually verified by the sanity check. Pinned indirectly by `TestScanGetRender::test_input_has_autofocus_and_name_code` (which runs on a fresh GET — the template is symmetric).
- **`maxlength="255"` on the code input** is conservative. The `Item.qr_code` column is `String(128)`; `Item.sku` is `String(64)`. A 255-char input is more lenient than either — a user pasting a longer string gets the input truncated client-side, but server-side validation would still 404 the lookup (no item has a 200-char sku). Acceptable; trims the failure mode.
- **`_resolve_code` helper is thin (two queries) but lives in the module rather than `app/items.py`** because it's scan-flow-specific shaping (the qr-then-sku precedence belongs to scanning, not to item CRUD). If a future surface (e.g. a barcode-driven stock-take walk) needs the same lookup, extract to `app/scan.py` as a public helper or to `app/items.py::resolve_by_code`. Flagged.
- **No nav highlight for `/admin/items/{id}/edit` arrived-via-scan.** The user lands on the items edit page after a scan, where the nav highlights "Items" via `request.url.path.startswith("/admin/items")`. They don't see "Scan" highlighted — that's correct, since they're no longer on `/scan`. A future polish slice could carry a "you scanned to get here" banner; deferred.
- **`_flash` helper duplicated** across `app/scan.py`, `app/locations.py`, `app/suppliers.py`, etc. — same one-liner six (now seven) times. Extracting to `app/template_env.py` would force a third-party import on every router that uses it. Acceptable at v1 scale; revisit if a flash-with-type (success/warning) ever lands. Same posture flagged in S1's self-critique.
- **`_resolve_code` doesn't case-fold.** A scanner physically reads what's printed; a user typing fallback typically types the SKU exactly as displayed (uppercase by convention in this codebase). If a future polish slice wants case-insensitive lookups, it's a one-line change to `func.lower(Item.qr_code) == code.lower()`. Deferred — none of the existing tests require case-folding, and the current uniqueness constraints are case-sensitive across the model (so two items can already exist with `sku="ABC"` and `sku="abc"`, and case-insensitive lookups would expose that ambiguity).

<!-- R5h plan (now shipped) — see Current state for the implementation summary; self-critique below.

Eighth CSV-export surface. Third *new* call site of R5e's `csv_branch` helper.
Pattern is now mechanical: ~10 LoC route extension + ~5 LoC template + ~21 tests
per new list-view surface. Cross-item checkouts admin joins variance trend +
PO list + items list + stock-takes list + suppliers list + locations list +
taxonomy list.

-->

---

**Self-critique notes (rolling) — R5h:**

- **Pattern is fully mechanical at eight surfaces.** Same shape as R5f/R5g: ~10 LoC route + ~5 LoC template + ~21 tests. Adding a ninth CSV surface (e.g. movements timeline, users list, reorder dashboard) is now copy-paste-modify. R5e's `csv_branch` helper continues to pay for itself: a new surface no longer thinks about magic strings, Content-Type, or sanitisation.
- **Eleven-column CSV is the wider end of the spectrum.** Prior surfaces ranged from 3 (taxonomy / locations) to 6 (PO list) to 10 (items list). The checkouts admin row has more state to surface — both checkout-side (id, dates, due/overdue) and item-side (sku, name, archived) plus the holder's email and the unique-unit serial (when present). The two `_id` columns (checkout_id + item_id) are explicit because they're the join keys to the rest of the system; including them keeps the CSV self-sufficient for office workflows that want to "find every checkout for item X" or "follow up on checkout Y" without re-joining against the HTML.
- **`is_overdue` separated from `days_overdue` in the CSV** (the HTML conflates them into a single "Status" cell). Rationale: a spreadsheet user who wants to filter "show me only overdue rows" needs a binary column; a user who wants to sort by urgency needs a numeric column. The CSV gives both. The `is_overdue=no → days_overdue=""` pairing is pinned by the test; the inverse (`yes → days_overdue.isdigit()`) is also pinned.
- **CSV body is time-sensitive** — `is_overdue` is computed from `datetime.now(UTC)` in `_list_open_checkouts`. A CSV downloaded at 23:59 UTC on day N might show different overdue values than one downloaded at 00:01 UTC on day N+1, even with no DB writes in between. This matches the HTML view (which is also computed at request time) and is consistent with the "snapshot artefact" framing of CSV exports. Documented; flagged as acceptable.
- **`expected_return` carries the full datetime in the CSV** vs. the HTML's `%Y-%m-%d` formatting. Rationale: a downstream consumer might want to sort by precise time-of-day (e.g. "tools due back this morning vs this afternoon"). The HTML's date-only is a UX choice (most checkouts are due back end-of-day); the CSV preserves the source-of-truth precision. Same posture as `checked_out_at` (always ISO datetime).
- **`unit_serial` + `holder_email` use empty string for None** (vs. the HTML's `—` em-dash). Sorting / filtering in spreadsheets is far more reliable on empty cells than on em-dashes; same posture as every prior surface that has nullable text columns.
- **No e2e walk for the CSV link.** Same posture as R5/R5b/R5c/R5d/R5f/R5g — Playwright doesn't simulate the OS file-save dialog, and the link visibility is pinned by integration tests. The existing `test_checkouts_e2e.py` walk already exercises the cross-item view's HTML page end-to-end (manager visits `/admin/checkouts` after C2/C3); clicking the CSV link would only re-test what the integration tests pin. Flagged.
- **Workshop gated to 403 at the dependency layer.** Pinned by `TestCheckoutsAdminCsvRoleEnforcement`'s 5 tests. Workshop is intentionally excluded from cross-item oversight (C4's design — Workshop sees per-item status blocks via C2's `/checkout` page, not the cross-item list). The CSV branch inherits this gate; same posture as the HTML branch.
- **CSV-injection mitigation still not applied.** Item names, SKUs, unit serials, and holder emails are all entered by managers / office or pulled from Google SSO sub-claims; recipients are office/manager colleagues with HTML access to the same data. Same v1 risk model as R5/R5b/R5c/R5d/R5f/R5g; the one-line `_coerce_cell` mitigation lands when the threat model changes. Documented.
- **`format` param shadows Python's `format()` builtin** — same wart as R5/R5b/R5c/R5d/R5f/R5g. Eight surfaces now, all shadowing. Renaming would break the URL convention. Acceptable.
- **Return type widened on `list_checkouts` from `HTMLResponse` to `Response`.** Necessary because the CSV branch returns a non-HTML `Response`. The `@router.get` decorator's `response_class` argument was dropped (only affects OpenAPI hint generation; runtime behaviour unchanged). The `HTMLResponse` import was removed entirely from `app/checkouts_admin.py` since no other route in the module uses it (unlike `app/taxonomy.py` which kept the import for the form routes). One less import to maintain.
- **No new helper module.** Header constant + rows helper sit in `app/checkouts_admin.py` next to the route — same shape as the seven prior surfaces. The cross-cutting concerns (filename sanitisation, cell coercion, Content-Type/Disposition shaping, the CSV-vs-HTML branch decision) all live in `app/csv_export.py`; the per-surface concerns (which columns, what filename pattern, what data shape) stay local. The split feels right at eight surfaces.
- **Sort survives the CSV branch.** `_list_open_checkouts` does its Python-side sort (overdue first, then `checked_out_at DESC, id DESC`) before returning; the CSV branch consumes the already-sorted list. The HTML and CSV both observe the same order — pinned indirectly by the show=overdue test (only the past-due row appears) and by the existing HTML ordering tests. Could add an explicit "two rows in CSV ordered overdue-first" test if a future regression were a concern; deferred as low-value given the helper's tests.

<!-- R5h plan (now shipped) — kept commented for audit-trail context only.

**R5h — CSV export on the cross-item checkouts admin list (DoD #7 polish, MISSION §3 "Export any list view to CSV"):** eighth CSV-export surface. Third *new* call site of R5e's `csv_branch` helper (after R5f's locations list + R5g's taxonomy list). Extends `app/checkouts_admin.py::list_checkouts` with a `?format=csv` query branch and adds a `checkouts-admin-csv-link` "Download CSV" link to `checkouts_admin.html`.

Plan:

- **Route extension** (`app/checkouts_admin.py::list_checkouts`):
  - New `format: str = ""` query param. `format == "csv"` triggers CSV via `csv_branch`; anything else (blank / `html` / garbage) renders HTML — same silent-coerce posture as `show`.
  - **Role gate inherited**: existing `Depends(require_role(Role.MANAGER, Role.OFFICE))` already blocks Workshop + pending at the dependency layer (Workshop excluded from the cross-item view per C4 — they have per-item status blocks via C2's `/checkout` page). Admin via the role bypass. No inner role-split needed.
  - Same data source as the HTML branch (`_list_open_checkouts(db, show=show, now=now)`); reuses the view-shaped dicts.
  - **Headers** (11 columns): `checkout_id`, `item_id`, `item_sku`, `item_name`, `item_archived`, `unit_serial`, `holder_email`, `checked_out_at`, `expected_return`, `is_overdue`, `days_overdue`. Mirrors the HTML table cells one-for-one (8 visual columns) plus three explicit ID/state columns: `checkout_id` + `item_id` (HTML carries them as `data-checkout-id` / `data-item-id` attributes; making them columns lets a downstream consumer join), and `is_overdue` (the HTML conflates it with `days_overdue` into a "Status" cell; the CSV separates them). The Actions cell (link) is presentation-only and not surfaced.
  - **`item_archived` + `is_overdue` cells**: render as the literal strings `"yes"` / `"no"` (matching R5/R5b's PO list `supplier_archived` and items list `requires_checkout` precedent — spreadsheet receivers find yes/no easier to filter on than `True`/`False`).
  - **`unit_serial` + `holder_email` cells**: empty when `None` (matching `csv_response`'s coercion). HTML renders `—` for these but a CSV cell of `—` would mis-sort against actual values.
  - **`checked_out_at`**: ISO datetime via `csv_response`'s coercion.
  - **`expected_return`**: ISO datetime when set, empty when None. The HTML formats as `%Y-%m-%d` but the CSV preserves the full datetime so a downstream consumer can sort precisely.
  - **`days_overdue`**: integer when overdue, empty when not. Matches the `is_overdue=no → days_overdue is None` pairing in `_list_open_checkouts`.
  - **Filename**: `checkouts_{show}.csv` — `checkouts_open.csv` / `checkouts_overdue.csv`. Coerced `show` is used so a user typing `?format=csv&show=garbage` gets `checkouts_open.csv`.
  - Module-level `_CHECKOUTS_ADMIN_CSV_HEADERS` constant + new `_csv_rows_for_checkouts(rows)` helper. Mirrors the seven prior surfaces' precedent.
  - **Return type widened** on `list_checkouts` from `HTMLResponse` to `Response`; `@router.get("", response_class=HTMLResponse)` decorator simplified to `@router.get("")`. `HTMLResponse` import dropped from the function signature only — no other route in the module uses it.
  - **Walrus form**: `if (resp := csv_branch(format, filename=..., headers=..., rows=...)) is not None: return resp` — same shape as the seven prior sites.

- **Template** (`checkouts_admin.html`): new `<a data-testid="checkouts-admin-csv-link" href="/admin/checkouts?format=csv&show={{ show }}">Download CSV</a>` link block sitting between the filter nav and the table. Href preserves active `show` value.

- **Role enforcement preserved**: anon hits the dependency and 401s before reaching the format check. Pending / Workshop hit the same dependency and 403.

- **Read-only invariant preserved**: GET-CSV writes no audit row (the route already writes no audit; CSV branch inherits this).

- **Test coverage** (target ~19 new in `tests/integration/test_checkouts_admin_routes.py`):
  - `TestCheckoutsAdminCsvRoleEnforcement` (5): anon 401; pending 403; Workshop 403; Manager 200; Office 200.
  - `TestCheckoutsAdminCsvHeaders` (3): Content-Type carries `text/csv; charset=utf-8`; default filename `checkouts_open.csv`; `?show=overdue` filename `checkouts_overdue.csv`.
  - `TestCheckoutsAdminCsvBody` (~7): empty emits header-only; one open qty-tracked row populated cells (including `is_overdue=no` + `days_overdue` empty + empty `unit_serial`); unique-tracked row carries unit serial; null user → empty `holder_email`; archived item → `item_archived=yes`; past-due → `is_overdue=yes` + `days_overdue=int`; show=overdue narrows to past-due only; returned checkouts excluded.
  - `TestCheckoutsAdminCsvHtmlBranch` (2): blank format renders HTML; unknown format renders HTML.
  - `TestCheckoutsAdminCsvReadOnly` (1): GET-CSV writes no audit row.
  - `TestCheckoutsAdminCsvLink` (2): link with `show=open` + `show=overdue` preserved.

-->

<!-- R5g plan (now shipped) — see Current state for the implementation summary; self-critique below.

Seventh CSV-export surface. Second *new* call site of R5e's `csv_branch` helper.
Pattern is now mechanical: ~8 LoC route extension + ~5 LoC template + ~19 tests
per new list-view surface. Taxonomy joins variance trend + PO list + items list
+ stock-takes list + suppliers list + locations list. Sub-category list is
deliberately out of scope (different per-parent shape; queued as R5h).

-->

---

**Self-critique notes (rolling) — R5g:**

- **Pattern is fully mechanical at seven surfaces.** Same shape as R5f: ~8 LoC route + ~5 LoC template + 19 tests. Adding an eighth CSV surface (e.g. movements list, users list, reorder dashboard, checkouts admin) is now copy-paste-modify. R5e's `csv_branch` helper continues to pay for itself: a new surface no longer thinks about magic strings, Content-Type, or sanitisation.
- **Sub-category list (`list_sub_categories`) deliberately excluded.** That route is per-parent (`/admin/taxonomy/{parent_id}/children`), so a single CSV would either need a parent-id-in-filename convention (`taxonomy_sub_{parent_id}_{show}.csv`) or scope-across-all-parents semantics (which the current route doesn't support). Trade-off: the per-parent CSV is mechanically the same as the top-level CSV (just one extra filter), but the URL convention divergence means it's a separate slice's worth of decisions. Queued informally as R5h. Flagged.
- **`leaf_ids` lookup ordering preserved.** The CSV branch sits *before* the `leaf_ids` query, so `?format=csv` skips that round-trip entirely. The HTML branch still runs it (no behaviour change for HTML). Net win: CSV is one DB query, HTML is two — same shape as R5f's locations CSV (locations also have no extra HTML-only query, but the principle holds).
- **`archived_at` not in CSV body.** Same posture as R5d / R5f — the filename encodes the active partition; an extra column would be redundant given the `?show=` filter. A user wanting both buckets in one file would have to download two files and concat. Acceptable for v1; flagged.
- **`created_at` / `updated_at` not in CSV.** The HTML view also hides these; the CSV mirrors HTML one-for-one. A historian wanting "when was each category added" hits the audit log instead. Same posture as R5d / R5f. Documented.
- **Sub-category exclusion test** (`test_sub_categories_not_in_csv`) — pins that the `parent_id IS NULL` filter survives any future refactor of the query. Without this, a refactor that accidentally widened the scope (e.g. removing the `parent_id` filter, or joining sub-cats in for a new feature) wouldn't fail the existing tests. Cheap insurance; worth it.
- **CSV-injection mitigation still not applied.** Category names are manager-typed; recipients are office/manager colleagues with HTML access to the same data. Same v1 risk model as R5/R5b/R5c/R5d/R5f; the one-line `_coerce_cell` mitigation lands when the threat model changes. Documented.
- **No e2e walk for the CSV link.** Same posture as R5f — Playwright doesn't simulate the OS file-save dialog, and the link visibility is pinned by integration tests. Existing `test_taxonomy_e2e.py` already exercises the HTML page end-to-end; clicking the CSV link would only re-test what the integration tests pin. Flagged.
- **Workshop + Office + Pending all gated to 403 at the dependency layer.** Pinned by `TestTaxonomyListCsvRoleEnforcement`'s six tests. The HTML page also doesn't render to those roles, so a "link absence" test isn't needed here — the link only renders when the page renders, and the page only renders to Manager + Admin. Same posture as R5d / R5f.
- **`format` param shadows Python's `format()` builtin** — same wart as R5/R5b/R5c/R5d/R5f. Seven surfaces now, all shadowing. Renaming would break the URL convention. Acceptable.
- **Return type widened on `list_taxonomy` from `HTMLResponse` to `Response`.** Necessary because the CSV branch returns a non-HTML `Response`. The `@router.get` decorator's `response_class` argument was dropped (only affects OpenAPI hint generation; runtime behaviour unchanged). No callers depend on the narrower type. `HTMLResponse` import retained — still used by `/new` + `/{id}/edit` + sub-category form routes.
- **No new helper module.** Header constant + rows helper sit in `app/taxonomy.py` next to the route — same shape as the six prior surfaces. The cross-cutting concerns (filename sanitisation, cell coercion, Content-Type/Disposition shaping, the CSV-vs-HTML branch decision) all live in `app/csv_export.py`; the per-surface concerns (which columns, what filename pattern, what data shape) stay local. The split feels right at seven surfaces.
- **`TaxonomyNode` ORM model passed directly to the rows helper** — same shape as R5d/R5f. No join + count needed (unlike R5's PO list); the helper just reads attributes. Documented.

Pattern is now mechanical: ~7 LoC route extension + ~5 LoC template + ~19 tests
per new list-view surface. Locations list joins variance trend + PO list +
