Mirrors the HTML table cells one-for-one (8 visual columns) plus three explicit ID/state columns: `checkout_id` + `item_id` are the join keys (HTML carries them as `data-checkout-id` / `data-item-id` attributes; making them columns lets a downstream consumer join), and `is_overdue` is separated from `days_overdue` (the HTML conflates them into a single "Status" cell; the CSV gives both a binary filter column and a numeric sort column). `item_archived` + `is_overdue` render as literal `"yes"`/`"no"` strings (matching R5/R5b's PO list `supplier_archived` + items list `requires_checkout` precedent). `unit_serial` + `holder_email` render as empty cells when None (vs. the HTML's `—` em-dash — empty sorts/filters cleaner in spreadsheets). `expected_return` carries the full datetime (the HTML formats as `%Y-%m-%d`; the CSV preserves source-of-truth precision). `days_overdue` is the integer when overdue, empty when not (matches `is_overdue=False → days_overdue is None` pairing in `_list_open_checkouts`). **Filename**: `checkouts_{show}.csv` — `checkouts_open.csv` / `checkouts_overdue.csv`. Coerced `show` is used so a user typing `?format=csv&show=garbage` gets `checkouts_open.csv`. **Module-level `_CHECKOUTS_ADMIN_CSV_HEADERS`** + new `_csv_rows_for_checkouts(rows)` helper. Mirrors the seven prior surfaces' precedent. **Return type widened** on `list_checkouts` from `HTMLResponse` to `Response`; `@router.get("", response_class=HTMLResponse)` decorator simplified to `@router.get("")`. The `HTMLResponse` import was removed entirely from `app/checkouts_admin.py` since no other route in the module used it (one fewer import to maintain — unlike `app/taxonomy.py` which kept the import for the form routes). **Walrus form**: `if (resp := csv_branch(format, filename=..., headers=..., rows=...)) is not None: return resp` — same shape as the seven prior sites. **Sort survives the CSV branch**: `_list_open_checkouts` does its Python-side sort (overdue first, then `checked_out_at DESC, id DESC`) before returning; the CSV branch consumes the already-sorted list. **Template**: new `<a data-testid="checkouts-admin-csv-link" href="/admin/checkouts?format=csv&show={{ show }}">Download CSV</a>` link block; href preserves active `show` value. Sits between the filter nav and the table. **Role enforcement preserved**: anon hits the dependency and 401s before reaching the format check; Pending / Workshop hit the same dependency and 403. **Read-only invariant preserved**: GET-CSV writes no audit row. **Time-sensitivity acknowledged**: `is_overdue` is computed from `datetime.now(UTC)` at request time; a CSV downloaded at 23:59 UTC vs 00:01 UTC the next day might differ even with no DB writes (consistent with the HTML view; consistent with the "snapshot artefact" framing of CSV exports). **Tests:** 21 new in `tests/integration/test_checkouts_admin_routes.py` — `TestCheckoutsAdminCsvRoleEnforcement` (5: anon 401, pending 403, Workshop 403, Manager 200, Office 200), `TestCheckoutsAdminCsvHeaders` (3: text/csv charset, default `checkouts_open.csv`, `?show=overdue` filename `checkouts_overdue.csv`), `TestCheckoutsAdminCsvBody` (8: header-only on empty, one open qty-tracked row with all 11 cells verified including `is_overdue=no` + empty `days_overdue` + empty `unit_serial`, unique-tracked carries unit serial, null user → empty `holder_email`, archived item → `item_archived=yes`, past-due → `is_overdue=yes` + `days_overdue` is positive int, show=overdue narrows to past-due only, returned checkouts excluded), `TestCheckoutsAdminCsvHtmlBranch` (2: blank + garbage format render HTML), `TestCheckoutsAdminCsvReadOnly` (1: GET-CSV writes no audit), `TestCheckoutsAdminCsvLink` (2: link renders for `show=open` and `show=overdue` with the active value preserved). Total pytest 1601 (was 1580, +21). 14 e2e (no count change — Playwright doesn't simulate the OS file-save dialog; the link visibility is already pinned by integration tests; existing `test_checkouts_e2e.py` already exercises the cross-item HTML page end-to-end). ruff + mypy clean (27 source files, no new modules). | 38 | R4 — Stock-take variance trend report (DoD #7) | `71f877a` | New module `app/reports.py` mounted at `/admin/reports`. One route this slice (R5 CSV will live alongside). Aggregates per row: `lines_with_variance` (count), `positive_variance` (sum of variance > 0), `negative_variance_abs` (sum of `abs(variance)` where < 0), `net_variance` (signed sum), `abs_variance` (sum of absolute values). Invariant `abs_variance == positive + negative_abs` pinned by unit test. **Totals card** sums per-side aggregates across in-window stock takes plus a `stock_take_count` counter. Always renders, even when zero rows (consistent framing). Newest-first ordering by `completed_at DESC, id DESC`. **Why "committed only"**: a `StockTakeLine.variance` is written by ST2 the moment a count is typed, but until ST3 commits, no adjustment movement exists in the cost engine. | 37 | ST3 — Commit stock-take variances as adjustment movements (DoD #5) | `6c1df76` | Closes DoD #5 — Office can now run a stock take end-to-end (schedule from ST1 → start + count + see variance from ST2 → commit from ST3). New route `POST /admin/stock-takes/{stock_take_id}/commit` on `app/stock_takes.py` for **Manager + Office** (Workshop + pending → 401/403; anon 401). Walks every line with non-zero variance, builds one `StockMovement(type=ADJUSTMENT)` per line via the cost engine: `record_receipt(..., source=POSITIVE_ADJUSTMENT)` for positive variance (creates layer + bumps qty); `consume_fifo` for negative variance (creates consumption rows + decrements qty). `stock_movements.stock_take_id` is now actively populated (FK had been live since ST1's migration but never written until ST3). Flips `StockTakeLine.committed=True` per non-zero-variance line. Sets `StockTake.completed_at = now()`. Writes one `stock_take.committed` audit row with `before={"completed_at": null}`, `after={"completed_at": <ISO>, "movements": [{line_id, item_id, movement_id, variance (str), direction, unit_cost (str | null), total_cost (str)}, ...]}`. 303s back to detail page (now in completed state). **Engine ownership preserved**: route never mutates `cost_layers.qty_remaining`, `item.current_qty`, `movement.total_cost`, or `cost_layer_consumptions.*` directly — the engine is the single owner. Caller pattern matches M2/M3/M4: `db.add(movement); db.flush(); engine_call(...)`. **Validation order** (atomic): 404 → 400 not-in-progress → 400 no-variances → per-positive-variance line `unit_cost_<id>` parses as non-negative Decimal (blank required → 400; non-numeric / negative → 400; zero allowed). **Atomic-on-raise**: insufficient stock on a negative-variance line raises `InsufficientStockError` *before any layer mutation* (M1 invariant). Route catches it, calls `db.rollback()` (drops every successful in-flight movement / layer / consumption / `committed` flag from the same transaction), re-loads the stock take, re-renders the detail page with HTTP 400 + `<p data-testid="stock-take-commit-error" role="alert">` block + the operator's typed `unit_cost_<id>` inputs preserved via `commit_form_values`. Pinned by `TestCommitInsufficientStock::test_partial_failure_leaves_no_state` — even if the first (positive) line would have succeeded in isolation, the second (negative) line's shortage rolls the whole transaction back. **Default unit cost** for positive-variance lines: `_last_unit_cost(db, item_id)` (newest layer's `unit_cost`; `ORDER BY received_at DESC, id DESC LIMIT 1`; same shape as PO2's helper). Items with no prior layers render an empty input. **Audit `total_cost` decimal scale wart**: positive carries `"7.500000"` (qty scale 4 × form-cost scale 2 = scale 6); negative carries `"4.00000000"` (qty scale 4 × layer-cost scale 4 = scale 8). Same wart as M3/M4. **All commit-batch movements share `reason="stock take #{N}"`**; per-line nuance lives on the audit row's `movements` list. **Helpers** (`_can_commit`, `_last_unit_cost`, `_parse_unit_cost_for_commit`, `_lines_with_non_zero_variance`). **`_detail_context` extended**: in-progress branch now carries `commit_lines` (variance rows with direction + pre-filled unit_cost_default) + optional `commit_error` + `commit_form_values`; line view dict gains `is_committed` flag. **Templates** (`stock_take_detail.html`): in-progress branch grows new "Commit" sub-section below the count form (`stock-take-commit-form` with per-row `stock-take-commit-row` carrying `data-direction` — positive renders `stock-take-commit-unit-cost-input`, negative renders `stock-take-commit-unit-cost-na`); zero-variance state shows `stock-take-no-variances-note`; completed branch's per-line row gains `data-committed="true|false"` + a 7th cell `stock-take-line-committed`. **Tests:** 49 new (18 unit in `tests/unit/test_stock_takes.py::TestCanCommit/TestLastUnitCost/TestParseUnitCostForCommit/TestLinesWithNonZeroVariance` + 31 integration in `tests/integration/test_stock_takes_routes.py::TestCommitRoleEnforcement/TestCommitValidation/TestCommitPositiveHappyPath/TestCommitNegativeHappyPath/TestCommitMixed/TestCommitInsufficientStock/TestCommitAuditShape/TestCommitFormRendering/TestCommittedBadgeOnCompleted`). Total pytest 1383 (was 1334, +49). 14 e2e (unchanged count; the existing `test_office_schedules_a_stock_take` walk is extended in-place to also commit and verify `current_qty` drops 50.0000 → 48.0000 via the cost engine's FIFO consume). ruff + mypy clean (25 source files, no new modules). | 30 | R1 — Reporting dashboard with FIFO valuation, low-stock count, top consumed, COGS (DoD #7) | `666e7c1` | First link in DoD #7's chain. New module `app/dashboard.py` with one route `GET /admin/dashboard` for **Manager + Office** (Admin via the bypass; Workshop + pending 403 — MISSION §3 "Workshop... cannot see aggregated cost data or reports"). Read-only — no mutations, no audit, no movement type, no new tables. **Aggregations** (each is a single round-trip): total inventory value = `SUM(qty_remaining * unit_cost)` across active items' open `cost_layers` rows (joined to `items` filtered `archived_at IS NULL`); low-stock count = `COUNT(items)` where `archived_at IS NULL AND current_qty <= reorder_threshold`; open POs count = `COUNT(purchase_orders)` where `status IN (draft, sent, partially_received)`; overdue checkouts = hardcoded 0 with `<small>` "checkouts not yet implemented" note (C-series will replace it; pinning the test-id `dashboard-overdue-checkouts` now means C-series doesn't have to re-template); top consumed = `SUM(qty)` over `stock_movements WHERE type=OUT AND created_at >= now() - top_days` grouped by `item_id`, joined to `items`, ordered desc, LIMIT 10 (window via `?top_days=N` defaulting 30; clamped `[1, 365]`; non-int / out-of-range silently coerce to default — same posture as M6 pagination); COGS = `SUM(total_cost)` over `stock_movements` where `id IN (SELECT DISTINCT movement_id FROM cost_layer_consumptions) AND created_at BETWEEN cogs_start AND cogs_end+1d` (consumption-row subquery covers OUT + negative-adjustment ADJUSTMENT — both go through `consume_fifo`; adjustment-increase has no consumption row so it's correctly excluded; IN has total_cost set but no consumption row; TRANSFER has neither). The COGS date range is end-inclusive (resolves to `[start 00:00 UTC, end+1 00:00 UTC)`). Default range: last 30 days. Bad-format ISO date 400. **Helpers**: `_coerce_top_days(raw)` (silent coerce on bad / out-of-range), `_parse_cogs_date(raw, *, field_name)` (400 on bad format; blank → None), `_resolve_cogs_range(start, end)` (defaults end=today, start=end-30d). Five aggregation helpers (`_total_inventory_value`, `_low_stock_count`, `_open_pos_count`, `_top_consumed`, `_cogs`) are pure DB reads — no side effects, no Request, no HTTPException. **Decimal coercion**: `func.coalesce(func.sum(...), 0)` returns Decimal under SQLAlchemy's `Numeric(14,4)` round-trip but mypy types `scalar_one()` as Any; defensively branch `if isinstance(total, Decimal): return total else Decimal(str(total))`. The `Decimal(str(...))` lands when SQLite reports SUM as int (all-zero-rows case). Both paths produce a deterministic Decimal output with no precision loss. **Templates / test-ids**: new `dashboard.html` with at-a-glance card row (`dashboard-heading`, `dashboard-total-value`, `dashboard-low-stock-count`, `dashboard-open-pos-count`, `dashboard-overdue-checkouts`); top-consumed table (`dashboard-top-consumed-table` + per-row `dashboard-top-consumed-row` with `data-item-id` + cells `dashboard-top-consumed-sku` / `dashboard-top-consumed-name` / `dashboard-top-consumed-qty` / `dashboard-top-consumed-detail-link`; empty state `dashboard-top-consumed-empty`); two filter forms (`dashboard-top-days-form` + `dashboard-top-days-input` + `dashboard-top-days-submit`; `dashboard-cogs-form` + `dashboard-cogs-start-input` + `dashboard-cogs-end-input` + `dashboard-cogs-submit`); COGS card (`dashboard-cogs-amount`). Each filter form carries the *other* param as a hidden input so submitting one preserves the other's value. `base.html` gains a `nav-dashboard` link (between Home and Suppliers) visible to Admin / Manager / Office; Workshop hidden. The `aria-current` is on `path == "/admin/dashboard" or startswith("/admin/dashboard/")` (same tightening pattern as PO2's `nav-reorder` fix). **Tests** (37 new — 32 in `tests/integration/test_dashboard_routes.py` + 5 in `tests/integration/test_layout.py` + 1 e2e walk in `test_dashboard_e2e.py`): `TestDashboardRoleEnforcement` (6) — anon 401; window excludes 100-day-old OUT (default 30-day); `?top_days=200` includes the 100-day-old OUT; `?top_days=foo` coerces to 30; `?top_days=99999` coerces to 30; TRANSFER not counted; `TestDashboardCOGS` (8) — zero with no movements; | 23 | M5 — Transfer between locations (no cost change) (DoD #3 partial, DoD #5 partial) | `33aa662` | Closes out the cost-engine call-site matrix: TRANSFER is the **only** `MovementType` that bypasses the engine, by design (no qty change → no cost change). New routes `GET /admin/items/{item_id}/transfer` + `POST /admin/items/{item_id}/transfer` mounted on the existing `app/movements.py` router for **Manager + Office + Workshop** (same matrix as M2 / M3 / M4 / M6). The route flips `item.location_id` from the current value to the user-picked target, records a `StockMovement(type=TRANSFER, total_cost=None)`, writes a `stock_movement.transfer` audit row, commits — never calls the cost engine, never creates a `CostLayer`, never writes a `CostLayerConsumption`, never mutates `item.current_qty`. Verified by three engine-isolation tests that seed a layer + run a transfer + assert the layer count + qty_remaining + current_qty are all unchanged. **Validation** (all 400 *before* any DB write — atomic): item exists (404), not archived (400), has a current `location_id` set (400 with "this item has no location yet — set one via the edit form before transferring"); `to_location_id` parses as int and references an *active* `Location` (archived rejects with "target location is not active"); `to_location_id` differs from current `location_id` (no-op transfers reject — would write a confusing audit row); `qty` parses as a positive Decimal (reuses `_parse_positive_decimal`). `reason` and `note` are optional, stripped, blank → None — same as M2 / M3; M4 differs because adjustments require attribution, transfers don't. **Audit shape**: `action="stock_movement.transfer"`, `entity_type="stock_movement"`, `entity_id=movement.id`, `before={"location_id": from_location_id}`, `after={"item_id", "qty", "from_location_id", "to_location_id", "reason", "note"}`. The `before` carries only the changed field on the *Item* (location_id), keeping the diff narrow and consistent with `item.updated`. The `after` carries the route inputs plus the resolved from/to ids so the row is self-contained for reporting (a future "by-location movement report" can read this row without joining back to movement + item). `from_location_id` appears in both `before` and `after` — that's deliberate, not a bug. **No `total_cost`, no `unit_cost`, no `source`, no `received_at`** — transfer rows don't carry any of those, consistent with the contract. **Form**: `qty` defaults to `current_qty` (most transfers are wholesale). For v1's single-location-per-item data model, the qty is informational on the movement row only — the location pointer flips wholesale regardless. Documented in the form's `<em>recorded for audit; transfers don't change current quantity or valuation</em>` hint. Partial-qty transfers across multiple "stock-by-location" rows is a v2 multi-location feature; out of scope for v1 per MISSION §3 "between locations (if multi-location is enabled)". **No in-form 400 carve-out** (unlike M3 / M4): every M5 validation error is a "user typed something wrong" case (parse error, out-of-options, same-as-current), not a data-dependent runtime error like M3's insufficient-stock. The bare-400 page is the right posture, matching every other validation 400 in the app outside M3 / M4's data-dependent stock-shortage carve-out. **M6 timeline integration**: TRANSFER rows render with no direction sign — `_attach_directions_and_breakdown`'s defensive `else` branch (already in place from M6) leaves `direction = ""` for movements that don't go through the engine. The `data-direction=""` attribute lets future styling distinguish them. The `total_cost` cell shows "—" via the existing `{% if m.total_cost is not none %}` template logic. **No layer-breakdown sub-row** appears for transfers (since the engine never wrote a consumption row for them). | 17 | M1 — `cost_layers` + `cost_layer_consumptions` + `stock_movements` + FIFO consumption engine (DoD #5, #6 prerequisite) | `2cd2c6c` | Pure-logic slice — no routes, no UI, no e2e. New `app/cost_engine.py` exposes `record_receipt`, `consume_fifo`, `open_value`, and `InsufficientStockError`. The engine is the **single owner** of `item.current_qty`, `cost_layers.qty_remaining`, and `stock_movements.total_cost` going forward — every M2-M6 / PO5 / ST-series route must call into it rather than mutate those columns directly. New ORM models in `app/models.py`: `StockMovement` (with `MovementType` enum: in/out/adjustment/transfer), `CostLayer` (with `CostLayerSource` enum: po_receipt/manual_in/positive_adjustment), `CostLayerConsumption`. Migration `0010_create_cost_layers_and_movements.py` adds the three tables in dependency order (movements first, then layers, then consumptions — consumptions FK into both layers and movements). **Schema deviation from MISSION §6**: `stock_movements.po_id` and `stock_take_id` are plain `Integer` columns with **no FK constraint** in M1, because `purchase_orders` and `stock_takes` don't exist yet. The FK constraint is a one-line addition in PO2 / ST1's migrations. Documented on the model. **No `archived_at` on any of the three new tables**: they're append-only by mission (§3 "Cost layer history is part of the audit trail and cannot be edited. Corrections are made via new movements"). The engine *does* mutate `cost_layers.qty_remaining` on consumption — that's the one exception, called out in the model docstring (running balance vs frozen received qty). **No DB-level immutability triggers** on the new tables (the audit-log triggers stay scoped to `audit_log` only): the engine is the only writer, and the route layer (M2+) won't expose UPDATE/DELETE paths. If a future "data correction" backdoor is ever added, that's the time to add triggers. **Engine contract**: caller creates the `StockMovement` row, flushes for id, then calls into the engine. Engine takes the movement as input (rather than constructing one) so the route layer owns actor / reason / type / note / po_id wiring. Engine sets `movement.total_cost` as a side effect. Engine raises `ValueError` for input violations (qty <= 0, unit_cost < 0, unflushed movement) and `InsufficientStockError(item_id, requested, available)` for over-consume. **Atomicity** of `consume_fifo`: the available-qty pre-check happens before any mutation, so a raise leaves the DB exactly as it was — verified by `test_over_consumption_is_atomic`. **FIFO order**: `(received_at ASC, id ASC)` — backdated receipts can land ahead of existing layers (e.g. invoice arrives late), and ties broken deterministically by id (verified by `test_ties_broken_by_id_when_received_at_identical` using `freezegun` to force the timestamp tie). The composite `ix_cost_layers_item_received` covers the ORDER BY. **`current_qty` ownership**: chosen "engine owns it" over "route owns it". The alternative invites every M2/M3/M4 route to redo the same arithmetic and risk drift. The engine is the only place that can compute `total_cost` correctly (FIFO sum), so co-locating `current_qty` mutation makes the inventory-level invariant atomic with the cost-level one. The I3 self-critique entry "current_qty not updated when units are created or archived" is now fixable — the M2 route for unique-tracked stock-in will go through the engine and bump `current_qty`. The historical wart (existing unique items show 0 until a movement fires) is still present; a one-shot backfill is M2's call. **No audit-log writes inside the engine**: that's the route's responsibility. The engine is below the audit layer. **No route-level integration in M1**: M2-M6 each add a route that wraps the engine. **Tests**: 44 new (15 in `tests/unit/test_cost_models.py` covering defaults + enum round-trips + FK NOT NULLs + qty_remaining-vs-qty_received independence + plain-Integer po_id/stock_take_id; 29 in `tests/unit/test_cost_engine.py` covering: receipt 9 (correct fields, current_qty increment, total_cost set, received_at default + override, qty/unit_cost validation matrix incl. zero-cost-allowed, unflushed-movement-rejected); single-layer consume 2 (partial + exact); multi-layer consume 3 (FIFO across two layers, exhausted-layer skipped, id-tiebreak with frozen time); errors 6 (over-consume raises with carried-fields, atomic-on-raise, no-layers-at-all, zero qty, negative qty, unflushed movement); isolation 1 (sibling items don't cross-consume); open_value 6 (empty, single, multi-source-sum, exhausted-excluded, partial-included, isolation); combined 2 (full receipt→consume→receipt→consume cycle + positive→negative adjustment cycle). 620 unit+integration (was 576, +44). 9 e2e unchanged. ruff + mypy clean (16 source files; +1 — `app/cost_engine.py`). Migration applies upgrade + downgrade cleanly against a fresh SQLite DB. |

New `FieldType` `StrEnum` with seven values (`text, number, decimal, date, boolean, select, multiselect`), stored as `SAEnum(..., values_callable=lambda cls: [e.value for e in cls])` to match the `Role`/`UserStatus` convention (the migration's column is `String(16)` which is what SAEnum boils down to with `native_enum=False`). **Leaf invariant**: a top-level node is a leaf iff it has no *active* children; a sub-category is always a leaf. Field-def creation + unarchive both 400 if the target isn't a leaf or is an archived node. **Cross-cutting guard**: `app/taxonomy.py` now imports `has_active_field_defs` and 400s `GET/POST /admin/taxonomy/{parent_id}/children/new\|''` when the parent has active field defs (forces the "archive defs first, then add sub-cats" workflow; archived defs do NOT block sub-cat creation — they're history, not schema). **Key auto-derivation** in `_derive_key`: `re.sub(r"[^a-z0-9]+", "_", name.lower()).strip("_")`. Empty after derive → 400. The audit diff records both `name` and `key` when a rename shifts the slug; casing-only renames keep the slug intact and only `name` appears in the diff. **Options validation**: `_parse_options` parses textarea blobs line-by-line (strip + drop empty + reject duplicates). Required for select/multiselect (400 if empty); rejected for other types (400 if any). **Required flag**: HTML checkbox with explicit `value="true"`; absent in form data ⇒ False. **sort_order**: same convention as nodes — blank-on-create steps by 10, blank-on-edit keeps existing. **Audit vocabulary**: `taxonomy_field_def.{created,updated,archived,unarchived}`. **Templates**: new `taxonomy_field_defs_list.html` (active/archived tabs, parent breadcrumb, "non-leaf" + "archived node" notes that hide the CTA when applicable, columns: order/name/type/required/options) and `taxonomy_field_def_form.html` (name + type select + options textarea + required checkbox + sort_order). `taxonomy_list.html` updated to render a per-row "Fields" link only when `n.id in leaf_ids` (server-computed in `list_taxonomy`); `taxonomy_children_list.html` renders the "Fields" link unconditionally on every sub-cat row. 76 new tests (`tests/unit/test_field_defs.py` 10: model defaults + options round-trip + per-node uniqueness for both name + key, both spanning archived; `tests/integration/test_field_defs_routes.py` 66 across 6 classes — `TestFieldDefRoleEnforcement` 7, `TestFieldDefList` 8 (incl. non-leaf-note + archived-node-note), `TestFieldDefCreate` 22 (full validation matrix incl. key auto-derive, key collision via casing rename, options-required-for-select/multiselect, options-rejected-for-non-select, options-with-duplicates, required-checkbox-true/unchecked, blank-sort-step-by-10, leaf invariant, audit content), `TestFieldDefEdit` 9 (rename re-derives slug, casing-only rename keeps key, type+options change, required toggle, blank-sort keeps existing, audit-diff-only-changed, name+key change recorded together, no-op no audit, sibling clash 400), `TestFieldDefArchive` 9 (idempotent archive + audit, idempotent unarchive, unknown 404, leaf-re-check on unarchive, archived-node block on unarchive), `TestSubCategoryCreateGuardedByActiveFieldDefs` 3) + e2e extension (5 new steps after the existing sub-cat walk: create "Karat" select with options 9/14/18 + required, archive, archived tab, unarchive). 384 unit+integration + 7 e2e passing. ruff + mypy clean (13 source files; `app/field_defs.py` added). |
| 10 | S4 — Taxonomy: sub-categories under a category (Manager-owned) | `cb19de3` | Sub-category routes added to `app/taxonomy.py` alongside the existing top-level routes. URL shapes: `GET /admin/taxonomy/{parent_id}/children[?show=…]` (per-parent list with active/archived tabs), `GET /admin/taxonomy/{parent_id}/children/new` (form, scoped by parent), `POST /admin/taxonomy/{parent_id}/children` (create), and four flat `/sub/{node_id}` routes for edit/update/archive/unarchive. The flat URL on edit/archive/unarchive avoids a "URL parent vs DB parent" mismatch (the handler verifies `parent_id IS NOT NULL` and 404s otherwise; URL parent doesn't have to match the actual parent). New helpers in `app/taxonomy.py`: `_check_child_name_unique(parent_id, name, exclude_id?)` (sibling-scoped 400 friendlier than a DB IntegrityError 500), `_next_child_sort_order(parent_id)` (mirror of `_next_top_sort_order`), `_get_top_level_parent` (loads parent, 404 if missing, 400 if the candidate is itself a sub-cat — the depth-limit guard), `_get_sub_category` (loads node, 404 if missing or top-level). Archived-parent guard: `GET …/children/new` and `POST …/children` both 400 when the parent is archived ("no new structure under archived"); existing sub-cats remain editable + archivable + unarchivable underneath an archived parent (cleanup, not new structure) — explicitly tested. Audit vocabulary unchanged: `taxonomy_node.{created,updated,archived,unarchived}` reused; the `created` row's `after.parent_id` carries the actual parent id for sub-cats (was hard-coded `None` for top-level, kept that way). New template `taxonomy_children_list.html`. `taxonomy_form.html` reused with new optional `parent` and `back_url` context vars: heading and CTA text adapt accordingly, and an "&larr; Back" link points at the right list. Top-level `taxonomy_list.html` gains a "Manage" link per row that drills into `/admin/taxonomy/{n.id}/children`. Route-pattern collisions: none — `/admin/taxonomy/{node_id}/{archive,unarchive,edit}` uses different literals than `/admin/taxonomy/{parent_id}/children[/new]`, and `/admin/taxonomy/sub/{node_id}/…` uses a literal `sub` segment that doesn't match any existing pattern. 46 new integration tests (`TestSubCategoryRoleEnforcement` 5; `TestSubCategoryList` 6; `TestSubCategoryCreate` 16 — happy, whitespace-strip, blank-sort steps-by-10, blank-sort zero on first, empty-name, duplicate-sibling, duplicate-archived-sibling, same-name-different-parent, same-name-as-top-level, unknown-parent 404, depth-violation 400, archived-parent 400, audit-row-with-parent_id, archived-parent-form-GET 400, list-show-archived; `TestSubCategoryEdit` 9; `TestSubCategoryArchive` 10) + e2e extension (after the existing top-level walk, manager clicks "Manage" → drills into Raw Materials' sub-cats → creates "Silver" → archives → tab to archived → unarchive). 308 unit+integration + 7 e2e passing. ruff + mypy clean (12 source files). |
| 9 | S3 — Taxonomy: top-level categories CRUD (Manager-owned) | `981a8aa` | New Manager-only `/admin/taxonomy` server-rendered CRUD: list (active/archived tabs, ordered by `sort_order` then name), new, create, edit, update (with field-level audit diff), archive, unarchive. Migration `0005_create_taxonomy_nodes.py` adds the `taxonomy_nodes` table with self-referencing nullable `parent_id` (ON DELETE RESTRICT — soft-delete only), `sort_order` (int default 0), and two partial unique indexes: `uq_taxonomy_top_name` on `(name)` where `parent_id IS NULL` and `uq_taxonomy_child_name` on `(parent_id, name)` where `parent_id IS NOT NULL`. Both indexes span archived rows (matches Supplier/Location convention: archiving doesn't free the name). The same partial indexes are declared in `TaxonomyNode.__table_args__` so `Base.metadata.create_all` (used by unit tests) creates them too. New `app/taxonomy.py` router with `_FIELDS=("name","sort_order")`, a `_check_top_name_unique` helper that filters by `parent_id IS NULL`, a `_next_top_sort_order` that returns `max(existing) + 10` (or 0 if empty), and a `_normalise` that parses `sort_order` to int (400 on non-integer). | 8 | S2.5 — Extract shared `app.template_env` (drop `init_templates` plumbing) | `139d4f8` | Refactor only — no behaviour change.
